DAN/EWR Date: 4/19/2025
A.B. No. 519—Creates a separate chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes
governing certain agencies and organizations that provide
nonmedical services. (BDR 40-805)
*A_AB519_451*
Page 1 of 88
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 3
ASSEMBLY BILL NO. 519–COMMITTEE ON
HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES
MARCH 24, 2025
_______________
Referred to Committee on Health and Human Services
SUMMARY—Creates a separate chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes governing
certain agencies and organizations that provide nonmedical
services. (BDR 40-805)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: No.
Effect on the State: Yes.
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to health care; establishing separate provisions for the licensing
or certification, regulation and discipline of agencies to provide
personal care services in the home, employment agencies that contract
to provide certain nonmedical services and intermediary service
organizations; enacting provisions to facilitate the collecting of certain
debts from applicants for certain licenses; imposing certain
requirements as an applicant for a certificate to operate an intermediary
service organization; revising the training requirements for certain
caregivers who receive reimbursement through Medicaid;
authorizing a family member to serve as the personal care
assistant for a recipient of Medicaid under certain circumstances;
providing penalties; and providing other matters properly relating
thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 Existing law provides for the licensure and regulation of various types of medical
2 facilities and facilities for the dependent by the Division of Public and Behavioral Health of
3 the Department of Health and Human Services. (Chapter 449 of NRS) Existing law requires
4 an agency to provide personal care services in the home to be licensed by the Division as a
5 facility for the dependent. (NRS 449.0045, 449.030) Existing law requires an employment
6 agency that contracts with persons in this State to provide nonmedical services related to
7 personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home to obtain a license
8 from the State Board of Health. (NRS 449.03005) Existing law requires an intermediary
9 service organization to obtain a certificate from the Division. (NRS 449.431) Existing law
10 requires the Board to adopt regulations governing agencies to provide personal care services
11 in the home, employment agencies that contract to provide nonmedical services related to
12 personal care to elderly persons and persons with disabilities and intermediary service
13 organizations. (NRS 449.03005, 449.0302, 449.4309)
14 This bill transfers the provisions of law governing agencies to provide personal care
15 services in the home, employment agencies that contract to provide nonmedical services
16 related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home and
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 4
17 intermediary service organizations from the chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes that
18 generally governs medical facilities and facilities for the dependent to a new chapter in the
19 Nevada Revised Statutes without changing the current substantive provisions that govern such
20 agencies and organizations. Sections 2-19, 24-49, 51-60, 69-79 and 81-90 of this bill create a
21 new chapter consisting of provisions for the licensure and regulation of such entities in a
22 manner substantially identical to the manner in which those entities are licensed and
23 regulated under existing law. Sections 94, 96-104 and 150 of this bill eliminate provisions
24 governing those entities from the chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes that regulates
25 medical facilities and facilities for the dependent. Sections 93, 111, 113, 117, 118, 120-123,
26 126-133, 138 and 146 of this bill eliminate references to sections repealed by section 150.
27 Sections 91, 92, 95 and 105-146 of this bill make various conforming changes so that the
28 legal status of agencies to provide personal care services in the home, employment agencies
29 that contract to provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or
30 persons with disabilities in the home and intermediary service organizations is not changed by
31 this bill.
32 Existing federal law requires each state to adopt procedures to ensure that applicants for
33 certain licenses and certificates comply with child support obligations, including by requiring
34 an applicant for such a license to provide his or her social security number. (42 U.S.C. § 666)
35 Sections 20, 21 and 50 of this bill enact such procedures as applicable to an applicant for the
36 issuance or renewal of a license to operate an agency to provide personal care services in the
37 home or an employment agency that contracts to provide nonmedical services related to
38 personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home in order to comply
39 with federal law. Section 23 of this bill establishes alternate provisions for such an applicant
40 who does not have a social security number. Section 22 of this bill also requires an applicant
41 for the renewal of such a license to provide certain information for the purpose of identifying
42 persons who owe certain debts to the State. Sections 65, 69, 74 and 76 of this bill establish
43 similar provisions for intermediary service organizations, which were carried over from
44 existing law. (NRS 449.4312, 449.4313, 449.4315, 449.432, 449.4322)
45 Existing law requires: (1) an agency to provide personal care services in the home to file
46 with the Administrator of the Division a surety bond or a substitute for a surety bond; and (2)
47 an applicant for a license to operate an agency to provide personal care services in the home to
48 undergo a criminal background check. (NRS 449.065, 449.067, 449.122) Sections 67, 68 and
49 80 of this bill impose similar requirements on intermediary service organizations.
50 Existing law requires: (1) the Department to apply for a home and community-
51 based services waiver to include structured family caregiving for certain persons as
52 medical assistance under Medicaid; and (2) a caregiver providing care under that waiver
53 to complete training required by the Aging and Disability Services Division of the
54 Department. (NRS 422.3965) Sections 30 and 122 of this bill instead require such a
55 caregiver to complete the same training that is required for unlicensed caregivers who
56 provide care for an agency to provide personal care services in the home.
57 Existing law requires the Director of the Department to include in the State Plan for
58 Medicaid authorization for a recipient of Medicaid to be deemed a provider of services
59 for the purposes of allowing the recipient to receive reimbursement for personal care
60 services covered by Medicaid and using that money to pay for services provided by a
61 personal care assistant or an agency to provide personal care services in the home. (NRS
62 422.272407). Section 120 of this bill authorizes a family member of a recipient of
63 Medicaid to serve as a personal care assistant for a recipient of Medicaid if the family
64 member: (1) completes the training required by section 30 for certain other caregivers;
65 and (2) receives authorization from a provider of health care.
66 Section 147 of this bill requires the Legislative Counsel to move regulations specifically
67 relating to such entities to a new chapter of the Nevada Administrative Code that corresponds
68 to the new chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes created by sections 2-90. Section 147 also:
69 (1) requires the Board to adopt new regulations to replace other regulations relating to those
70 entities that remain in the chapter of the Nevada Administrative Code governing medical
71 facilities and facilities for the dependent; and (2) provides that those existing regulations
72 remain in effect until the Board adopts new regulations to replace them. Section 148 of this
73 bill clarifies that this bill does not affect the validity of: (1) licenses or certificates to operate
74 agencies to provide personal care services in the home, employment agencies that contract to
75 provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 5
76 disabilities in the home and intermediary service organizations; (2) certain training completed
77 by the operators, employees and contractors of such entities; or (3) disciplinary actions taken
78 against such entities.
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:
1 Section 1. Title 40 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto a new
2 chapter to consist of the provisions set forth as sections 2 to 90, inclusive, of this
3 act.
4 Sec. 2. As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires, the
5 words and terms defined in sections 3 to 7, inclusive, of this act have the
6 meanings ascribed to them in those sections.
7 Sec. 3. 1. “Agency to provide personal care services in the home” means
8 any person, other than a natural person, which provides services authorized
9 pursuant to section 52 of this act to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in
10 the home.
11 2. The term does not include:
12 (a) An independent contractor who provides nonmedical services specified in
13 section 52 of this act without the assistance of employees;
14 (b) An organized group of persons composed of the family and friends of a
15 person needing nonmedical services related to personal care that employs or
16 contracts with persons to provide such nonmedical services for the person if:
17 (1) The organization of the group of persons is set forth in a written
18 document that is made available for review by the Division upon request; and
19 (2) The services are provided to only one person or one family who
20 resides in the same residence;
21 (c) An intermediary service organization; or
22 (d) A person or agency that contracts with the Aging and Disability Services
23 Division of the Department of Health and Human Services to provide temporary
24 respite services.
25 3. As used in this section:
26 (a) “Intermediary service organization” has the meaning ascribed to it in
27 section 59 of this act.
28 (b) “Temporary respite services” means services provided through a contract
29 with the Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health and
30 Human Services to a natural person on a periodic basis to provide a respite for a
31 regular provider of services.
32 Sec. 4. “Board” means the State Board of Health.
33 Sec. 5. “Division” means the Division of Public and Behavioral Health of
34 the Department of Health and Human Services.
35 Sec. 6. “Employment agency” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS
36 611.020.
37 Sec. 7. “Nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or
38 persons with disabilities” includes, without limitation:
39 1. The elimination of wastes from the body;
40 2. Dressing and undressing;
41 3. Bathing;
42 4. Grooming;
43 5. The preparation and eating of meals;
44 6. Laundry;
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 6
1 7. Shopping;
2 8. Cleaning;
3 9. Transportation; and
4 10. Any other minor needs related to the maintenance of personal hygiene.
5 Sec. 8. Except as otherwise provided in section 12 of this act, no person,
6 state or local government or agency thereof may operate or maintain in this State
7 an agency to provide personal care services in the home without first obtaining a
8 license as provided in sections 8 to 58, inclusive, of this act.
9 Sec. 9. 1. Except as otherwise provided in section 12 of this act, a person
10 must obtain a license from the Board to operate an employment agency that
11 contracts with persons in this State to provide nonmedical services related to
12 personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home,
13 regardless of whether the employment agency is located in this State.
14 2. The Board shall adopt:
15 (a) Standards for licensing of employment agencies that contract to provide
16 nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with
17 disabilities in the home;
18 (b) Standards relating to the fees charged by such employment agencies;
19 (c) Regulations governing the licensing of such employment agencies; and
20 (d) Regulations establishing requirements for training the persons who
21 contract with such employment agencies to provide such nonmedical services.
22 3. An employment agency that is licensed pursuant to this section shall not
23 refer a person to a home to provide nonmedical services related to personal care
24 to elderly persons or persons with disabilities if that person has not met the
25 requirements set forth in sections 36 to 40, inclusive, of this act.
26 4. A person who violates the provisions of subsection 3 is liable for a civil
27 penalty to be recovered by the Attorney General in the name of the Board for the
28 first offense of not more than $10,000 and for a second and subsequent offense
29 of not less than $10,000 nor more than $20,000. Unless otherwise required by
30 federal law, the Board shall deposit all civil penalties collected pursuant to this
31 section into a separate account in the State General Fund to be used to
32 administer and carry out the provisions of chapter 449A of NRS and sections 2 to
33 58, inclusive, of this act and to protect the health, safety, well-being and property
34 of the persons served by the employment agencies.
35 Sec. 10. 1. The Division shall develop and implement a process by which
36 a person with a criminal history may petition the Division to review the criminal
37 history of the person to determine if the person’s criminal history will disqualify
38 the person from obtaining a license pursuant to sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this
39 act.
40 2. Not later than 90 days after a petition is submitted to the Division
41 pursuant to subsection 1, the Division shall inform the person of the
42 determination of the Division of whether the person’s criminal history will
43 disqualify the person from obtaining a license. The Division is not bound by its
44 determination of disqualification or qualification and may rescind such a
45 determination at any time.
46 3. The Division may provide instructions to a person who receives a
47 determination of disqualification to remedy the determination of disqualification.
48 A person may resubmit a petition pursuant to subsection 1 not earlier than 6
49 months after receiving instructions pursuant to this subsection if the person
50 remedies the determination of disqualification.
51 4. A person with a criminal history may petition the Division at any time,
52 including, without limitation, before obtaining any education or paying any fee
53 required to obtain a license from the Division.
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 7
1 5. A person may submit a new petition to the Division not earlier than 2
2 years after the final determination of the initial petition submitted to the Division.
3 6. The Division may impose a fee of up to $50 upon the person to fund the
4 administrative costs in complying with the provisions of this section. The Division
5 may waive such fees or allow such fees to be covered by funds from a scholarship
6 or grant.
7 7. The Division may post on its Internet website:
8 (a) The requirements to obtain a license pursuant to sections 2 to 58,
9 inclusive, of this act from the Division; and
10 (b) A list of crimes, if any, that would disqualify a person from obtaining a
11 license from the Division.
12 8. The Division may request the criminal history record of a person who
13 petitions the Division for a determination pursuant to subsection 1. To the extent
14 consistent with federal law, if the Division makes such a request of a person, the
15 Division shall require the person to submit his or her criminal history record
16 which includes a report from:
17 (a) The Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History; and
18 (b) The Federal Bureau of Investigation.
19 9. A person who petitions the Division for a determination pursuant to
20 subsection 1 shall not submit false or misleading information to the Division.
21 10. The Division shall, on or before the 20th day of January, April, July
22 and October, submit to the Director of the Legislative Counsel Bureau in an
23 electronic format prescribed by the Director, a report that includes:
24 (a) The number of petitions submitted to the Division pursuant to subsection
25 1;
26 (b) The number of determinations of disqualification made by the Division
27 pursuant to subsection 1;
28 (c) The reasons for such determinations; and
29 (d) Any other information that is requested by the Director or which the
30 Division determines would be helpful.
31 11. The Director shall transmit a compilation of the information received
32 pursuant to subsection 10 to the Legislative Commission quarterly, unless
33 otherwise directed by the Commission.
34 Sec. 11. The provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act do not
35 apply to any agency to provide personal care services in the home that is operated
36 and maintained by the United States Government or an agency thereof.
37 Sec. 12. A person who is licensed or certified pursuant to a provision of this
38 chapter other than section 9 of this act or a provision of chapter 449 of NRS and
39 who contracts with persons to provide nonmedical services related to personal
40 care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities is not required to obtain an
41 additional license pursuant to section 9 of this act.
42 Sec. 13. 1. The Board shall adopt:
43 (a) Licensing standards for agencies to provide personal care services in the
44 home.
45 (b) Regulations governing the licensing of such agencies.
46 (c) Regulations that prescribe the specific types of discrimination prohibited
47 by section 32 of this act.
48 (d) Any other regulations as it deems necessary or convenient to carry out
49 the provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act.
50 2. The Board shall require that the practices and policies of each agency to
51 provide personal care services in the home provide adequately for the protection
52 of the health, safety and physical, moral and mental well-being of each person
53 served by the agency.
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 8
1 Sec. 14. 1. The Board shall adopt regulations authorizing an employee of
2 an agency to provide personal care services in the home, with the consent of the
3 person receiving services, to:
4 (a) Check, record and report the temperature, blood pressure, apical or
5 radial pulse, respiration or oxygen saturation of a person receiving services from
6 the agency;
7 (b) Using an auto-injection device approved by the Food and Drug
8 Administration for use in the home, administer to a person receiving services
9 from the agency insulin furnished by a registered pharmacist, as directed by a
10 physician, physician assistant or advanced practice registered nurse, or assist
11 such a person with the self-administration of such insulin; and
12 (c) Using a device for monitoring blood glucose approved by the Food and
13 Drug Administration for use in the home, conduct a blood glucose test on a
14 person receiving services from the agency or assist such a person to conduct a
15 blood glucose test on himself or herself.
16 2. The regulations adopted pursuant to this section:
17 (a) Must require the tasks described in subsection 1 to be performed in
18 conformance with the Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments of 1988,
19 Public Law No. 100-578, 42 U.S.C. § 263a, if applicable, and any other
20 applicable federal law or regulation;
21 (b) Must prohibit the use of a device for monitoring blood glucose on more
22 than one person; and
23 (c) May require a person to receive training before performing any task
24 described in subsection 1.
25 Sec. 15. 1. Money received from the licensing of agencies to provide
26 personal care services in the home must be forwarded to the State Treasurer for
27 deposit in the State General Fund to the credit of the Division.
28 2. The Division shall enforce the provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of
29 this act and may incur any necessary expenses not in excess of money authorized
30 for that purpose by the State or received from the Federal Government.
31 Sec. 16. The Division may:
32 1. Upon receipt of an application for a license, conduct an investigation
33 into the qualifications of personnel, methods of operation, policies and purposes
34 of any person proposing to engage in the operation of an agency to provide
35 personal care services in the home.
36 2. Upon receipt of a complaint against an agency to provide personal care
37 services in the home, except for a complaint concerning the cost of services,
38 conduct an investigation into the qualifications of personnel, methods of
39 operation, policies, procedures and records of that agency or any other such
40 agency which may have information pertinent to the complaint.
41 3. Employ such professional, technical and clerical assistance as it deems
42 necessary to carry out the provisions of this chapter.
43 Sec. 17. 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section, the Division may
44 charge and collect from an agency to provide personal care services in the home
45 or a person who operates such an agency without a license issued by the Division
46 the actual costs incurred by the Division for the enforcement of the provisions of
47 this chapter, including, without limitation, the actual cost of conducting an
48 inspection or investigation of the agency.
49 2. The Division shall not charge and collect the actual cost for enforcement
50 pursuant to subsection 1 if the enforcement activity is:
51 (a) Related to the issuance or renewal of a license for which the Board
52 charges a fee pursuant to sections 19 and 28 of this act; or
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 9
1 (b) Conducted pursuant to an agreement with the Federal Government
2 which has appropriated money for that purpose.
3 3. Any money collected pursuant to subsection 1 may be used by the
4 Division to administer and carry out the provisions of this chapter and the
5 regulations adopted pursuant thereto.
6 Sec. 18. Any person, state or local government or agency thereof desiring a
7 license under the provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act, must file
8 with the Division an application, on a form prescribed, prepared and furnished by
9 the Division, containing:
10 1. The name of the applicant and, if a natural person, whether the applicant
11 has attained the age of 21 years.
12 2. The address of the principal place of business of the agency.
13 3. In specific terms, the nature of services and type of care to be offered, as
14 defined in the regulations.
15 4. The name of the person in charge of the agency.
16 5. Such other information as may be required by the Division for the proper
17 administration and enforcement of this chapter.
18 6. Evidence satisfactory to the Division that the applicant is of reputable
19 and responsible character. If the applicant is a firm, association, organization,
20 partnership, business trust, corporation or company, similar evidence must be
21 submitted as to the members thereof and the person in charge of the agency for
22 which the application is made. If the applicant is a political subdivision of the
23 State or other governmental agency, similar evidence must be submitted as to the
24 person in charge of the entity for which application is made.
25 7. Evidence satisfactory to the Division of the ability of the applicant to
26 comply with the provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act and the
27 standards and regulations adopted by the Board.
28 Sec. 19. Each application for a license must be accompanied by such fee as
29 may be determined by regulation of the Board. The Board may, by regulation,
30 allow or require payment of a fee for a license in installments and may fix the
31 amount of each payment and the date that the payment is due.
32 Sec. 20. An application for the issuance of a license pursuant to sections 2
33 to 58, inclusive, of this act must include the social security number of the
34 applicant.
35 Sec. 21. 1. An applicant for the issuance or renewal of a license pursuant
36 to sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act must submit to the Division the statement
37 prescribed by the Division of Welfare and Supportive Services of the Department
38 of Health and Human Services pursuant to NRS 425.520. The statement must be
39 completed and signed by the applicant.
40 2. The Division shall include the statement required pursuant to subsection
41 1 in:
42 (a) The application or any other forms that must be submitted for the
43 issuance or renewal of the license; or
44 (b) A separate form prescribed by the Division.
45 3. A license may not be issued or renewed by the Division pursuant to
46 sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act if the applicant:
47 (a) Fails to submit the statement required pursuant to subsection 1; or
48 (b) Indicates on the statement submitted pursuant to subsection 1 that the
49 applicant is subject to a court order for the support of a child and is not in
50 compliance with the order or a plan approved by the district attorney or other
51 public agency enforcing the order for the repayment of the amount owed
52 pursuant to the order.
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 10
1 4. If an applicant indicates on the statement submitted pursuant to
2 subsection 1 that the applicant is subject to a court order for the support of a
3 child and is not in compliance with the order or a plan approved by the district
4 attorney or other public agency enforcing the order for the repayment of the
5 amount owed pursuant to the order, the Division shall advise the applicant to
6 contact the district attorney or other public agency enforcing the order to
7 determine the actions that the applicant may take to satisfy the arrearage.
8 Sec. 22. 1. In addition to any other requirements set forth in sections 2 to
9 58, inclusive, of this act, an applicant for the renewal of a license pursuant to
10 those sections must indicate in the application submitted to the Division whether
11 the applicant has a state business license. If the applicant has a state business
12 license, the applicant must include in the application the business identification
13 number assigned by the Secretary of State upon compliance with the provisions
14 of chapter 76 of NRS.
15 2. A license issued pursuant to sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act may
16 not be renewed by the Division if:
17 (a) The applicant fails to submit the information required by subsection 1; or
18 (b) The State Controller has informed the Division pursuant to subsection 5
19 of NRS 353C.1965 that the applicant owes a debt to an agency that has been
20 assigned to the State Controller for collection and the applicant has not:
21 (1) Satisfied the debt;
22 (2) Entered into an agreement for the payment of the debt pursuant to
23 NRS 353C.130; or
24 (3) Demonstrated that the debt is not valid.
25 3. As used in this section:
26 (a) “Agency” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 353C.020.
27 (b) “Debt” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 353C.040.
28 Sec. 23. 1. The Division shall not deny the application of a person for a
29 license pursuant to sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act based solely on his or
30 her immigration status.
31 2. Notwithstanding the provisions of section 20 of this act, an applicant for
32 a license pursuant to sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act who does not have a
33 social security number must provide an alternative personally identifying
34 number, including, without limitation, his or her individual taxpayer
35 identification number, when completing an application for such a license.
36 3. The Division shall not disclose to any person who is not employed by the
37 Division the social security number or alternative personally identifying number,
38 including, without limitation, his or her individual taxpayer identification
39 number, of an applicant for a license for any purpose except:
40 (a) Tax purposes;
41 (b) Licensing purposes; and
42 (c) Enforcement of an order for the payment of child support.
43 4. A social security number or alternative personally identifying number,
44 including, without limitation, an individual taxpayer identification number,
45 provided to the Division is confidential and is not a public record for the purposes
46 of chapter 239 of NRS.
47 Sec. 24. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6 and section 25 of
48 this act, each agency to provide personal care services in the home, when
49 applying for a license or renewing a license, file with the Administrator of the
50 Division of Public and Behavioral Health a surety bond:
51 (a) If the agency employs less than 7 employees, in the amount of $5,000;
52 (b) If the agency employs at least 7 but not more than 25 employees, in the
53 amount of $25,000; or
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 11
1 (c) If the agency employs more than 25 employees, in the amount of $50,000.
2 2. A bond filed pursuant to this section must be executed by the agency as
3 principal and by a surety company as surety. The bond must be payable to the
4 Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health and Human
5 Services and must be conditioned to provide indemnification to an older client
6 who the Attorney for the Rights of Older Persons and Persons with a Physical
7 Disability, an Intellectual Disability or a Related Condition determines has
8 suffered property damage as a result of any act or failure to act by the agency to
9 protect the property of the older client.
10 3. Except when a surety is released, the surety bond must cover the period
11 of the initial license to operate or the period of the renewal, as appropriate.
12 4. A surety on any bond filed pursuant to this section may be released after
13 the surety gives 30 days’ written notice to the Administrator of the Division of
14 Public and Behavioral Health, but the release does not discharge or otherwise
15 affect any claim filed by an older client for property damaged as a result of any
16 act or failure to act by the agency to protect the property of the older client
17 alleged to have occurred while the bond was in effect.
18 5. A license is suspended by operation of law when the agency is no longer
19 covered by a surety bond as required by this section or by a substitute for the
20 surety bond pursuant to section 25 of this act. The Administrator of the Division
21 of Public and Behavioral Health shall give the agency at least 20 days’ written
22 notice before the release of the surety or the substitute for the surety, to the effect
23 that the license will be suspended by operation of law until another surety bond
24 or substitute for the surety bond is filed in the same manner and amount as the
25 bond or substitute being terminated.
26 6. The requirement of filing a surety bond set forth in this section does not
27 apply to an agency to provide personal care services in the home that is operated
28 and maintained by the State of Nevada or an agency thereof.
29 7. As used in this section, “older client” means a client who is 60 years of
30 age or older.
31 Sec. 25. 1. As a substitute for the surety bond required pursuant to
32 section 24 of this act, an agency to provide personal care services in the home
33 may deposit with any bank or trust company authorized to do business in this
34 State, upon approval from the Administrator of the Division of Public and
35 Behavioral Health:
36 (a) An obligation of a bank, savings and loan association, savings bank,
37 thrift company or credit union licensed to do business in this State;
38 (b) Bills, bonds, notes, debentures or other obligations of the United States or
39 any agency or instrumentality thereof, or guaranteed by the United States; or
40 (c) Any obligation of this State or any city, county, town, township, school
41 district or other instrumentality of this State, or guaranteed by this State, in an
42 aggregate amount, based upon principal amount or market value, whichever is
43 lower.
44 2. The obligations of a bank, savings and loan association, savings bank,
45 thrift company or credit union must be held to secure the same obligation as
46 would the surety bond required by section 24 of this act. With the approval of the
47 Administrator of the Division of Public and Behavioral Health, the depositor may
48 substitute other suitable obligations for those deposited, which must be assigned
49 to the Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health and
50 Human Services and are negotiable only upon approval by the Administrator of
51 the Aging and Disability Services Division.
52 3. Any interest or dividends earned on the deposit accrue to the account of
53 the depositor.

1 4. The deposit must be an amount at least equal to the surety bond required

5 Sec. 26. 1. The Division shall issue a license to operate an agency to
6 provide personal care services in the home if, after investigation, the Division
7 finds that the applicant is in:
8 (a) Full compliance with the provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this
9 act; and
10 (b) Substantial compliance with the standards and regulations adopted by the
11 Board.
12 2. A license applies only to the person to whom it is issued and is not
13 transferable.
14 Sec. 27. Each license issued by the Division to an agency to provide
15 personal care services in the home must be in the form prescribed by the Division
16 and must contain:
17 1. The name of the person or persons authorized to operate the agency to
18 provide personal care services in the home; and
19 2. The nature of services offered and the capacity of the licensee to deliver
20 services.
21 Sec. 28. 1. Each license to operate an agency to provide personal care
22 services in the home issued pursuant to sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act
23 expires on December 31 following its issuance and is renewable for 1 year upon
24 reapplication and payment of all fees required pursuant to subsection 3 and
25 section 19 of this act unless the Division finds, after an investigation, that the
26 agency has not satisfactorily complied with the provisions of sections 2 to 58,
27 inclusive, of this act, or the standards and regulations adopted by the Board.
28 2. Each reapplication for an agency to provide personal care services in the
29 home must include, without limitation:
30 (a) A statement that the agency is in compliance with the provisions of
31 sections 36 to 40, inclusive, and 49 of this act; and
32 (b) A statement that the holder of the license, the administrator or other
33 person in charge and employees of the agency are in compliance with the
34 provisions of section 31 of this act.
35 3. Each reapplication for an agency to provide personal care services in the
36 home must be accompanied by the fee prescribed by the Board pursuant to NRS
37 457.240, in addition to the fees imposed pursuant to section 19 of this act.
38 Sec. 29. 1. The Division may cancel the license of an agency to provide
39 personal care services in the home and issue a provisional license, effective for a
40 period determined by the Division, to such an agency if the agency:
41 (a) Is in operation at the time of the adoption of standards and regulations
42 pursuant to the provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act, and the
43 Division determines that the agency requires a reasonable time under the
44 particular circumstances within which to comply with the standards and
45 regulations; or
46 (b) Has failed to comply with the standards or regulations and the Division
47 determines that the agency is in the process of making the necessary changes or
48 has agreed to make the changes within a reasonable time.
49 2. The provisions of subsection 1 do not require the issuance of a license or
50 prevent the Division from refusing to renew or from revoking or suspending any
51 license where the Division deems such action necessary for the health and safety
52 of the persons receiving services from any agency.

32 Sec. 31. 1. An applicant for a license to operate an agency to provide
33 personal care services in the home must receive training to recognize and prevent
34 the abuse of older persons before a license to operate such an agency is issued to
35 the applicant. If an applicant has completed such training within the year
36 preceding the date of the application for a license and the application includes
37 evidence of the training, the applicant shall be deemed to have complied with the
38 requirements of this subsection.
39 2. A licensee who holds a license to operate an agency to provide personal
40 care services in the home must annually receive training to recognize and prevent
41 the abuse of older persons before the license to operate such an agency may be
42 renewed.
43 3. If an applicant or licensee who is required by this section to obtain
44 training is not a natural person, the person in charge of the agency must receive
45 the training required by this section.
46 4. An administrator or other person in charge of an agency to provide
47 personal care services in the home must receive training to recognize and prevent
48 the abuse of older persons before the agency provides care to a person and
49 annually thereafter.
50 5. An employee who will provide care for an agency to provide personal
51 care services in the home must receive training to recognize and prevent the
52 abuse of older persons before the employee provides care to a person in the
53 agency and annually thereafter.

1 6. The topics of instruction that must be included in the training required
2 by this section must include, without limitation:
3 (a) Recognizing the abuse of older persons, including sexual abuse and
4 violations of NRS 200.5091 to 200.50995, inclusive;
5 (b) Responding to reports of the alleged abuse of older persons, including
6 sexual abuse and violations of NRS 200.5091 to 200.50995, inclusive; and
7 (c) Instruction concerning the federal, state and local laws, and any changes
8 to those laws, relating to:
9 (1) The abuse of older persons; and
10 (2) Agencies to provide personal care services in the home for the person.
11 7. The agency to provide personal care services in the home is responsible
12 for the costs related to the training required by this section.
13 8. The holder of a license to operate an agency to provide personal care
14 services in the home shall ensure that each person who is required to comply with
15 the requirements for training pursuant to this section complies with those
16 requirements. The Division may, for any violation of this section, take

18 Sec. 32. 1. An agency to provide personal care services in the home and
19 any employee or independent contractor of such an agency shall not discriminate
20 in the provision of services to a client based wholly or partially on the actual or
21 perceived race, color, religion, national origin, ancestry, age, gender, physical or
22 mental disability, sexual orientation, gender identity or expression or human
23 immunodeficiency virus status of the client or any person with whom the client
24 associates.
25 2. An agency to provide personal care services in the home shall:
26 (a) Develop and carry out policies to prevent the specific types of prohibited
27 discrimination described in the regulations adopted by the Board pursuant to
28 section 13 of this act and meet any other requirements prescribed by regulations
29 of the Board; and
30 (b) Post prominently on any Internet website used to market the agency the
31 following statement:
32
33 [Name of the agency to provide personal care services in the home] does
34 not discriminate and does not permit discrimination, including, without
35 limitation, bullying, abuse or harassment, on the basis of actual or
36 perceived race, color, religion, national origin, ancestry, age, gender,
37 physical or mental disability, sexual orientation, gender identity or
38 expression or HIV status, or based on association with another person on
39 account of that person’s actual or perceived race, color, religion, national
40 origin, ancestry, age, gender, physical or mental disability, sexual
41 orientation, gender identity or expression or HIV status.
42
43 3. The provisions of this section shall not be construed to:
44 (a) Require an agency to provide personal care services in the home or an
45 employee or independent contractor thereof to take or refrain from taking any
46 action in violation of reasonable medical standards; or
47 (b) Prohibit an agency to provide personal care services in the home from
48 adopting a policy that is applied uniformly and in a nondiscriminatory manner,
49 including, without limitation, such a policy that bans or restricts sexual relations.
50 Sec. 33. An agency to provide personal care services in the home shall:
51 1. Maintain the confidentiality of personally identifiable information
52 concerning the sexual orientation of a client, whether the client is transgender or
53 has undergone gender-affirming surgery and the human immunodeficiency virus
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 15
1 status of the client and take reasonable actions to prevent the unauthorized
2 disclosure of such information;
3 2. Prohibit employees or independent contractors of the agency who are not
4 directly providing care to a client from being present during any portion of the
5 care, during which the client is fully or partially unclothed without the express
6 permission of the client or the authorized representative of the client;
7 3. Use visual barriers, including, without limitation, doors, curtains and
8 screens, to provide privacy for clients who are fully or partially unclothed; and
9 4. Allow a client to refuse to be examined or observed by or receive services
10 from an employee or independent contractor of the agency for a purpose that is
11 primarily educational rather than therapeutic.
12 Sec. 34. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, to enable an
13 agent or employee of an agency to provide personal care services in the home
14 who is described in subsection 2 to more effectively care for clients the Board
15 shall, by regulation, require such an agency to conduct training relating
16 specifically to cultural competency for any agent or employee of the agency who
17 is described in subsection 2 so that such an agent or employee may better
18 understand clients who have different cultural backgrounds, including, without
19 limitation, clients who are:
20 (a) From various racial and ethnic backgrounds;
21 (b) From various religious backgrounds;
22 (c) Persons with various sexual orientations and gender identities or
23 expressions;
24 (d) Children and senior citizens;
25 (e) Persons with a mental or physical disability; and
26 (f) Part of any other population that such an agent or employee may need to
27 better understand, as determined by the Board.
28  The Board shall set forth by regulation the frequency with which an agency to
29 provide personal care services in the home is required to provide such training
30 relating to cultural competency.
31 2. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, the requirements of
32 subsection 1 apply to any agent or employee of an agency to provide personal
33 care services in the home who:
34 (a) Provides personal care services or administrative or support services and
35 has direct client contact at least once each week on average as a part of his or her
36 regular job duties; or
37 (b) Oversees an agent or employee described in paragraph (a).
38 3. An agency to provide personal care services in the home is not required
39 to provide training relating specifically to cultural competency to an agent or
40 employee who is described in subsection 2 and who has successfully completed a
41 course or program in cultural competency as part of the continuing education
42 requirements for the agent or employee to renew his or her professional license,
43 registration or certificate, as applicable.
44 4. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6, the training relating
45 specifically to cultural competency conducted by an agency to provide personal
46 care services in the home pursuant to subsection 1 must be provided through a
47 course or program that is approved by the Department of Health and Human
48 Services.
49 5. The Office of Minority Health and Equity of the Department of Health
50 and Human Services shall ensure that the list established and maintained
51 pursuant to NRS 449.103 is distributed to each agency to provide personal care
52 services in the home which is required to conduct training relating specifically to
53 cultural competency pursuant to subsection 1.

11 Sec. 35. The Board shall adopt regulations that require an agency to
12 provide personal care services in the home to:
13 1. Develop policies to ensure that a client is addressed by his or her
14 preferred name and pronoun and in accordance with his or her gender identity or

22 Sec. 36. 1. Each applicant for a license to operate an agency to provide
23 personal care services in the home or employment agency that contracts with
24 persons to provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons
25 or persons with disabilities in the home shall submit to the Central Repository for
26 Nevada Records of Criminal History one complete set of fingerprints for
27 submission to the Federal Bureau of Investigation for its report.
28 2. The Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History shall
29 determine whether the applicant has been convicted of a crime listed in
30 paragraph (a) of subsection 1 of section 49 of this act and immediately inform the
31 administrator of the agency and the Division of whether the applicant has been
32 convicted of such a crime.
33 Sec. 37. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsections 2 and 3, within 10
34 days after hiring an employee, accepting an employee of a temporary employment
35 service or entering into a contract with an independent contractor, the
36 administrator of, or the person licensed to operate, an agency to provide personal
37 care services in the home or employment agency that contracts with persons to
38 provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or persons
39 with disabilities in the home shall:
40 (a) Obtain a written statement from the employee, employee of the temporary
41 employment service or independent contractor stating whether he or she has been
42 convicted of any crime listed in section 49 of this act;
43 (b) Obtain an oral and written confirmation of the information contained in
44 the written statement obtained pursuant to paragraph (a);
45 (c) Obtain proof that the employee, employee of the temporary employment
46 service or independent contractor holds any required license, permit or
47 certificate;
48 (d) Obtain from the employee, employee of the temporary employment
49 service or independent contractor one set of fingerprints and a written
50 authorization to forward the fingerprints to the Central Repository for Nevada
51 Records of Criminal History for submission to the Federal Bureau of
52 Investigation for its report;
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 17
1 (e) Submit to the Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History
2 the fingerprints obtained pursuant to paragraph (d) to obtain information on the
3 background and personal history of each employee, employee of a temporary
4 employment service or independent contractor to determine whether the person
5 has been convicted of any crime listed in section 49 of this act; and
6 (f) If an Internet website has been established pursuant to NRS 439.942:
7 (1) Screen the employee, employee of the temporary employment service
8 or independent contractor using the Internet website. Upon request of the

33 (a) The employee, employee of the temporary employment service or
34 independent contractor agrees to allow the administrator of, or the person

36 receive notice from the Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal
37 History regarding any conviction and subsequent conviction of the employee,
38 employee of the temporary employment service or independent contractor of a
39 crime listed in section 49 of this act;
40 (b) An agency, board or commission that regulates an occupation or

42 within the immediately preceding 5 years, submitted the fingerprints of the
43 employee, employee of the temporary employment service or independent
44 contractor to the Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History for
45 submission to the Federal Bureau of Investigation for its report; and
46 (c) The report of the Federal Bureau of Investigation indicated that the
47 employee, employee of the temporary employment service or independent
48 contractor has not been convicted of any crime set forth in section 49 of this act.

21 6. Upon receiving fingerprints submitted pursuant to this section, the
22 Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History shall determine
23 whether the employee, employee of the temporary employment service or
24 independent contractor has been convicted of a crime listed in section 49 of this
25 act and immediately inform the Division and the administrator of, or the person
26 licensed to operate, the agency to provide personal care services in the home or
27 employment agency that contracts with persons to provide nonmedical services
28 related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home

30 employment service or independent contractor has been convicted of such a
31 crime.
32 7. The Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History may
33 impose a fee upon an agency that submits fingerprints pursuant to this section
34 for the reasonable cost of the investigation. The agency to provide personal care
35 services in the home or employment agency that contracts with persons to provide
36 nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with
37 disabilities in the home may recover from the employee or independent contractor
38 whose fingerprints are submitted not more than one-half of the fee imposed by
39 the Central Repository. If the agency requires the employee or independent
40 contractor to pay for any part of the fee imposed by the Central Repository, it
41 shall allow the employee or independent contractor to pay the amount through
42 periodic payments. The agency may require a temporary employment service
43 which employs a temporary employee whose fingerprints are submitted to pay the
44 fee imposed by the Central Repository. An agency shall notify a temporary
45 employment service if a person employed by the temporary employment service is
46 determined to be ineligible to provide services at the agency based upon the
47 results of an investigation conducted pursuant to this section.
48 8. Unless a greater penalty is provided by law, a person who willfully
49 provides a false statement or information in connection with an investigation of
50 the background and personal history of the person pursuant to this section that
51 would disqualify the person from employment, including, without limitation, a
52 conviction of a crime listed in section 49 of this act, is guilty of a misdemeanor.

1 Sec. 38. 1. A temporary employment service shall not send an employee to

38 supervision before such information is received;
39 (b) During the period required pursuant to subsection 2 to allow the
40 employee, employee of the temporary employment service or independent
41 contractor to correct that information, except that an employee, employee of the
42 temporary employment service or independent contractor shall not have contact
43 with a child without supervision during such period;
44 (c) Based on the information received from the Central Repository, if the
45 information received from the Central Repository was inaccurate; or
46 (d) Any combination thereof.

51 Sec. 41. Any authorized member or employee of the Division may enter and

1 Sec. 42. Every agency to provide personal care services in the home may be
2 inspected at any time, with or without notice, as often as is necessary by:
3 1. The Division of Public and Behavioral Health to ensure compliance with
4 all applicable regulations and standards; and
5 2. Any person designated by the Aging and Disability Services Division of

8 Sec. 43. The Division shall prepare a report of the results of its inspections
9 of agencies to provide personal care services in the home regarding compliance
10 with applicable regulations and standards. The report must be provided to the
11 agency to provide personal care services in the home and include, without
12 limitation, a recommendation of the Division for correcting any deficiencies and,
13 if a deficiency is discovered as a result of an investigation by a county, district or
14 city board of health or health officer, the recommendations of the board or health
15 officer.
16 Sec. 44. 1. The Division may deny an application for a license or may
17 suspend or revoke any license to operate an agency to provide personal care
18 services in the home issued under the provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of
19 this act upon any of the following grounds:
20 (a) Violation by the applicant or the licensee of any of the provisions of NRS
21 449A.100 to 449A.124, inclusive, or sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act or of
22 any other law of this State or of the standards, rules and regulations adopted
23 thereunder.
24 (b) Aiding, abetting or permitting the commission of any illegal act.
25 (c) Conduct inimical to the public health, morals, welfare and safety of the
26 people of the State of Nevada in the maintenance and operation of the agency for
27 which a license is issued.
28 (d) Conduct or practice detrimental to the health or safety of the clients or
29 employees of the agency to provide personal care services in the home.
30 2. In addition to the provisions of subsection 1, the Division may revoke a
31 license to operate an agency to provide personal care services in the home if, with
32 respect to that agency, the licensee that operates the agency, or an agent or
33 employee of the licensee:
34 (a) Is convicted of violating any of the provisions of NRS 202.470;
35 (b) Is ordered to but fails to abate a nuisance pursuant to NRS 244.360,
36 244.3603 or 268.4124; or
37 (c) Is ordered by the appropriate governmental agency to correct a violation
38 of a building, safety or health code or regulation but fails to correct the violation.
39 3. The Division shall maintain a log of any complaints that it receives
40 relating to activities for which the Division may revoke the license to operate an
41 agency to provide personal care services in the home pursuant to subsection 2.
42 4. On or before February 1 of each odd-numbered year, the Division shall
43 submit to the Director of the Legislative Counsel Bureau a written report setting
44 forth, for the previous biennium:
45 (a) Any complaints included in the log maintained by the Division pursuant
46 to subsection 3; and
47 (b) Any disciplinary actions taken by the Division pursuant to subsection 2.
48 Sec. 45. 1. In addition to the payment of the amount required by section
49 17 of this act, if an agency to provide personal care services in the home violates
50 any provision related to its licensure, including any provision of sections 2 to 58,
51 inclusive, of this act or any condition, standard or regulation adopted by the
52 Board, the Division, in accordance with the regulations adopted pursuant to
53 section 46 of this act, may:
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 22
1 (a) Prohibit the agency to provide personal care services in the home from
2 providing services to a client until it determines that the agency has corrected the
3 violation;
4 (b) Except where a greater penalty is authorized by subsection 2, impose an
5 administrative penalty of not more than $5,000 per day for each violation,
6 together with interest thereon at a rate not to exceed 10 percent per annum; and
7 (c) Appoint temporary management to oversee the operation of the agency to
8 provide personal care services in the home and to ensure the health and safety of
9 the clients of the agency, until:
10 (1) It determines that the agency has corrected the violation and has
11 management which is capable of ensuring continued compliance with the
12 applicable statutes, conditions, standards and regulations; or
13 (2) Improvements are made to correct the violation.
14 2. If the agency to provide personal care services in the home fails to pay
15 any administrative penalty imposed pursuant to paragraph (b) of subsection 1,
16 the Division may:
17 (a) Suspend the license of the agency until the administrative penalty is paid;
18 and
19 (b) Collect court costs, reasonable attorney’s fees and other costs incurred to
20 collect the administrative penalty.
21 3. The Division may require any agency to provide personal care services in
22 the home that violates any provision of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act or
23 any condition, standard or regulation adopted by the Board to make any
24 improvements necessary to correct the violation.
25 4. Any money collected as administrative penalties pursuant to paragraph
26 (b) of subsection 1 must be accounted for separately and used to administer and
27 carry out the provisions of chapter 449A of NRS and sections 2 to 58, inclusive,
28 of this act to protect the health, safety, well-being and property of the clients in
29 accordance with applicable state and federal standards or for any other purpose
30 authorized by the Legislature.
31 Sec. 46. The Board shall adopt regulations establishing the criteria for the
32 imposition of each sanction prescribed by section 45 of this act. These regulations
33 must:
34 1. Prescribe the circumstances and manner in which each sanction applies;
35 2. Minimize the time between identification of a violation and the
36 imposition of a sanction;
37 3. Provide for the imposition of incrementally more severe sanctions for
38 repeated or uncorrected violations;
39 4. Provide for less severe sanctions for lesser violations of applicable state
40 statutes, conditions, standards or regulations; and
41 5. Establish an administrative penalty to be imposed if a violation of
42 sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act causes harm or the risk of harm to more
43 than one person.
44 Sec. 47. 1. When the Division intends to deny, suspend or revoke a
45 license, or impose any sanction prescribed by section 45 of this act, it shall give
46 reasonable notice to all parties by certified mail. The notice must contain the
47 legal authority, jurisdiction and reasons for the action to be taken. Notice is not
48 required if the Division finds that the public health requires immediate action. In
49 that case, it may order a summary suspension of a license pursuant to this section
50 and NRS 233B.127 or impose any sanction prescribed by section 45 of this act,
51 pending proceedings for revocation or other action.
52 2. If a person wants to contest the action of the Division, the person must
53 file an appeal pursuant to regulations adopted by the Board.
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 23
1 3. Upon receiving notice of an appeal, the Division shall hold a hearing
2 pursuant to regulations adopted by the Board.
3 4. The Board shall adopt such regulations as are necessary to carry out the
4 provisions of this section.
5 Sec. 48. 1. If the Division suspends the license of an agency to provide
6 personal care services in the home pursuant to the provisions of this chapter, or if
7 such an agency otherwise ceases to operate, including, without limitation,
8 pursuant to an action or order of a health authority pursuant to chapter 441A of
9 NRS, the Division may, if deemed necessary by the Administrator of the Division,
10 take control of and ensure the safety of the records of the agency.
11 2. Subject to the provisions of the Health Insurance Portability and
12 Accountability Act of 1996, Public Law 104-191, the Division shall:
13 (a) Maintain the confidentiality of the records obtained pursuant to
14 subsection 1.
15 (b) Share records obtained pursuant to subsection 1 with law enforcement
16 agencies in this State and other governmental entities which have authority to
17 license the agency to provide personal care services in the home or to license the
18 owners or employees of the agency.
19 (c) Release a record obtained pursuant to subsection 1 to the client or legal
20 guardian of the client who is the subject of the record.
21 3. The Board shall adopt regulations to carry out the provisions of this
22 section, including, without limitation, regulations for contracting with a person to
23 maintain any records under the control of the Division pursuant to subsection 1
24 and for payment by the agency to provide personal care services in the home of
25 the cost of maintaining medical records.
26 Sec. 49. 1. In addition to the grounds listed in section 44 of this act, the
27 Division or the Board, as applicable, may deny a license to operate an agency to
28 provide personal care services in the home or employment agency that contracts
29 with persons to provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly
30 persons or persons with disabilities in the home to an applicant or may suspend
31 or revoke the license of a licensee to operate such an agency if:
32 (a) The applicant or licensee has been convicted of:
33 (1) Murder, voluntary manslaughter or mayhem;
34 (2) Assault or battery with intent to kill or to commit sexual assault or
35 mayhem;
36 (3) Sexual assault, statutory sexual seduction, incest, lewdness or
37 indecent exposure, or any other sexually related crime that is punished as a
38 felony;
39 (4) Prostitution, solicitation, lewdness or indecent exposure, or any other
40 sexually related crime that is punished as a misdemeanor, within the immediately
41 preceding 7 years;
42 (5) A crime involving domestic violence that is punished as a felony;
43 (6) A crime involving domestic violence that is punished as a
44 misdemeanor, within the immediately preceding 7 years;
45 (7) Abuse or neglect of a child or contributory delinquency;
46 (8) A violation of any federal or state law regulating the possession,
47 distribution or use of any controlled substance or any dangerous drug as defined
48 in chapter 454 of NRS, within the immediately preceding 7 years;
49 (9) Abuse, neglect, exploitation, isolation or abandonment of older
50 persons or vulnerable persons, including, without limitation, a violation of any
51 provision of NRS 200.5091 to 200.50995, inclusive, or a law of any other
52 jurisdiction that prohibits the same or similar conduct;
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 24
1 (10) A violation of any provision of law relating to Medicaid or a law of
2 any other jurisdiction that prohibits the same or similar conduct, within the
3 immediately preceding 7 years;
4 (11) A violation of any provision of NRS 422.450 to 422.590, inclusive;
5 (12) A criminal offense under the laws governing Medicaid or Medicare,
6 within the immediately preceding 7 years;
7 (13) Any offense involving fraud, theft, embezzlement, burglary, robbery,
8 fraudulent conversion or misappropriation of property, within the immediately
9 preceding 7 years;
10 (14) Any other felony involving the use or threatened use of force or
11 violence against the victim or the use of a firearm or other deadly weapon; or
12 (15) An attempt or conspiracy to commit any of the offenses listed in this
13 paragraph, within the immediately preceding 7 years; or
14 (b) The licensee has, in violation of section 40 of this act, continued to
15 employ a person who has been convicted of a crime listed in paragraph (a).
16 2. In addition to the grounds listed in section 44 of this act, the Division or
17 the Board, as applicable, may suspend or revoke the license of a licensee to
18 operate an agency to provide personal care services in the home or employment
19 agency that contracts with persons to provide nonmedical services related to
20 personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home if the
21 licensee has, in violation of section 40 of this act, continued to employ a person
22 who has been convicted of a crime listed in paragraph (a) of subsection 1.
23 3. As used in this section:
24 (a) “Domestic violence” means an act described in NRS 33.018.
25 (b) “Medicaid” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 439B.120.
26 (c) “Medicare” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 439B.130.
27 Sec. 50. 1. If the Division receives a copy of a court order issued pursuant
28 to NRS 425.540 that provides for the suspension of all professional, occupational
29 and recreational licenses, certificates and permits issued to a person who is the
30 holder of license, the Division shall deem the license issued to that person to be
31 suspended at the end of the 30th day after the date on which the court order was
32 issued unless the Division receives a letter issued to the holder of the license by
33 the district attorney or other public agency pursuant to NRS 425.550 stating that
34 the holder of the license has complied with the subpoena or warrant or has
35 satisfied the arrearage pursuant to NRS 425.560.
36 2. The Division shall reinstate a license issued pursuant to sections 2 to 58,
37 inclusive, of this act that has been suspended by a district attorney pursuant to
38 NRS 425.540 if the Division receives a letter issued by the district attorney or
39 other public agency pursuant to NRS 425.550 to the person whose certificate was
40 suspended stating that the person whose license was suspended has complied with
41 the subpoena or warrant or has satisfied the arrearage pursuant to NRS 425.560.
42 Sec. 51. If a patient is released by a hospital to his or her residence to
43 receive care from an agency to provide personal care services in the home, the
44 agency to provide personal care services in the home shall consult with a
45 dietitian, as appropriate, to ensure that the patient or the person with primary
46 responsibility for the care of the patient understands the dietary needs of the
47 patient.
48 Sec. 52. An agency to provide personal care services in the home that is
49 licensed pursuant to this chapter may, through its employees or by contractual
50 arrangement with other persons, provide:
51 1. To persons with disabilities, any medical services authorized pursuant to
52 NRS 629.091; and
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 25
1 2. Nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or
2 persons with disabilities to assist those persons with activities of daily living.
3 Sec. 53. Any person who is employed by an agency to provide personal care
4 services in the home who:
5 1. Has successfully completed a course in cardiopulmonary resuscitation
6 according to the guidelines of the American National Red Cross or American
7 Heart Association;
8 2. Has successfully completed the training requirements of a course in
9 basic emergency care of a person in cardiac arrest conducted in accordance with
10 the standards of the American Heart Association; or
11 3. Has successfully completed the training requirements of a course in the
12 use and administration of first aid, including cardiopulmonary resuscitation,
13  and who in good faith renders emergency care or assistance in accordance
14 with the person’s training, in the course of his or her regular employment or
15 profession, to an elderly person or a person with a disability, is not liable for any
16 civil damages as a result of any act or omission, not amounting to gross
17 negligence, by that person in rendering that care.
18 Sec. 54. The name, sign, listing or other designation of an agency to
19 provide personal care services in the home must not contain any terms
20 misleading to the public with regard to the services offered.
21 Sec. 55. 1. An agency to provide personal care services in the home or an
22 employee of such an agency shall not:
23 (a) Refer a person to a residential facility for groups that is not licensed by
24 the Division; or
25 (b) Refer a person to a residential facility for groups if the agency to provide
26 personal care services in the home or its employee knows or reasonably should
27 know that the residential facility for groups, or the services provided by the
28 residential facility for groups, are not appropriate for the condition of the person
29 being referred.
30 2. If an agency to provide personal care services in the home or an
31 employee of such an agency violates the provisions of subsection 1, the agency to
32 provide personal care services in the home is liable for a civil penalty to be
33 recovered by the Attorney General in the name of the Board for the first offense
34 of not more than $10,000 and for a second or subsequent offense of not less than
35 $10,000 or more than $20,000. Unless otherwise required by federal law, the
36 Board shall deposit all civil penalties collected pursuant to this section into a
37 separate account in the State General Fund to be used for the enforcement of this
38 section and the protection of the health, safety, well-being and property of
39 residents of residential facilities for groups.
40 3. The Board shall:
41 (a) Establish and maintain a system to track violations of this section. Except
42 as otherwise provided in this paragraph, records created by or for the system are
43 public records and are available for public inspection. The following information
44 is confidential:
45 (1) Any personally identifying information relating to a person who is
46 referred to a residential facility for groups.
47 (2) Information which may not be disclosed under federal law.
48 (b) Educate the public regarding the requirements and prohibitions set forth
49 in this section and NRS 449.0305.
50 4. As used in this section, “residential facility for groups” has the meaning
51 ascribed to it in NRS 449.017.
52 Sec. 56. 1. In addition to the payment of the amount required by section
53 17 of this act and any civil penalty imposed pursuant to subsection 4, a person
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 26
1 who operates an agency to provide personal care services in the home without a

3 2. If the Division believes that a person is operating an agency to provide

5 an order to cease and desist the operation of the agency. The order must be
6 served upon the person by personal delivery or by certified or registered mail,
7 return receipt requested. The order is effective upon service.
8 3. If a person does not voluntarily cease operating an agency to provide
9 personal care services in the home without a license or apply for licensure within
10 30 days after the date of service of the order pursuant to subsection 2, the
11 Division may bring an action in a court of competent jurisdiction pursuant to
12 section 57 of this act.
13 4. Upon a showing by the Division that a person is operating an agency to
14 provide personal care services in the home without a license, a court of competent
15 jurisdiction may:
16 (a) Enjoin the person from operating the agency.
17 (b) Impose a civil penalty on the operator to be recovered by the Division of
18 not more than $10,000 for the first offense or not less than $10,000 or more than
19 $25,000 for a second or subsequent offense.
20 5. Unless otherwise required by federal law, the Division shall deposit all
21 civil penalties collected pursuant to paragraph (b) of subsection 4 into a separate
22 account in the State General Fund to be used to administer and carry out the
23 provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act and to protect the health,
24 safety, well-being and property of the clients in accordance with applicable state
25 and federal standards.

43 Sec. 59. As used in sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act, unless the
44 context otherwise requires, “intermediary service organization” means a
45 nongovernmental entity that provides services authorized pursuant to section 60
46 of this act for a person with a disability or other responsible person.
47 Sec. 60. 1. An intermediary service organization that is certified pursuant
48 to sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act may provide services for a person with a
49 disability or other responsible person relating to personal assistance received by
50 the person with a disability. The services that may be provided by an intermediary
51 service organization include, without limitation:
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 27
1 (a) Obtaining a criminal background check of a personal assistant selected
2 by the person with a disability or other responsible person to provide nonmedical
3 services and any medical services authorized pursuant to NRS 629.091;
4 (b) Providing payroll services to pay the personal assistant and determine
5 any tax liability;
6 (c) Providing services relating to financial management; and
7 (d) Providing any other services relating to the employment of a personal
8 assistant and any other financial assistance relating to the personal assistance for
9 the person with a disability.
10 2. As used in this section:
11 (a) “Other responsible person” means:
12 (1) A parent or guardian of, or any other person legally responsible for, a
13 person with a disability who is under the age of 18 years; or
14 (2) A parent, spouse, guardian or adult child of a person with a disability
15 who suffers from a cognitive impairment.
16 (b) “Personal assistance” means the provision of any goods or services to
17 help a person with a disability maintain his or her independence, personal
18 hygiene and safety, including, without limitation, the provision of services by a
19 personal assistant.
20 (c) “Personal assistant” means a person who, for compensation and under
21 the direction of a person with a disability or other responsible person, performs
22 services for a person with a disability to help the person maintain his or her
23 independence, personal hygiene and safety.
24 Sec. 61. 1. The Board shall adopt regulations authorizing an employee of
25 an intermediary service organization, with the consent of the person receiving
26 services, to:
27 (a) Check, record and report the temperature, blood pressure, apical or
28 radial pulse, respiration or oxygen saturation of a person receiving services from
29 the organization;
30 (b) Using an auto-injection device approved by the Food and Drug
31 Administration for use in the home, administer to a person receiving services
32 from the organization insulin furnished by a registered pharmacist as directed by
33 a physician or assist such a person with the self-administration of such insulin;
34 and
35 (c) Using a device for monitoring blood glucose approved by the Food and
36 Drug Administration for use in the home, perform a blood glucose test on a
37 person receiving services from the organization or assist such a person to
38 perform a blood glucose test on himself or herself.
39 2. The regulations adopted pursuant to this section:
40 (a) Must require the tasks described in subsection 1 to be performed in
41 conformance with the Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments of 1988,
42 Public Law No. 100-578, 42 U.S.C. § 263a, if applicable, and any other
43 applicable federal law or regulation;
44 (b) Must prohibit the use of a device for monitoring blood glucose on more
45 than one person; and
46 (c) May require a person to receive training before performing any task
47 described in subsection 1.
48 Sec. 62. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, a person shall
49 not operate or maintain in this State an intermediary service organization without
50 first obtaining a certificate to operate an intermediary service organization as
51 provided in sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act.
52 2. A person who is licensed to operate an agency to provide personal care
53 services in the home pursuant to this chapter is not required to obtain a
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 28
1 certificate to operate an intermediary service organization as described in this
2 section.
