4 misdemeanor.
5 Sec. 63. Any person wishing to obtain a certificate to operate an
6 intermediary service organization pursuant to the provisions of sections 59 to 90,
7 inclusive, of this act must file with the Division an application, on a form
8 prescribed, prepared and furnished by the Division, containing:
9 1. The name of the applicant and, if a person, whether the applicant has
10 attained the age of 21 years.
11 2. The location of the intermediary service organization.
12 3. The name of the person in charge of the intermediary service
13 organization.
14 4. Such other information as may be required by the Division for the proper
15 administration and enforcement of sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act.
16 5. Evidence satisfactory to the Division that the applicant is of reputable
17 and responsible character. If the applicant is a firm, association, organization,
18 partnership, business trust, corporation or company, similar evidence must be
19 submitted as to the members thereof, and the person in charge of the
20 intermediary service organization for which the application is made.
21 6. Evidence satisfactory to the Division of the ability of the applicant to
22 comply with the provisions of sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act and the
23 standards and regulations adopted by the Board.
24 Sec. 64. An application for the issuance of a certificate to operate an
25 intermediary service organization pursuant to section 63 of this act must include
26 the social security number of the applicant.
27 Sec. 65. 1. An applicant for the issuance or renewal of a certificate to
28 operate an intermediary service organization must submit to the Division the
29 statement prescribed by the Division of Welfare and Supportive Services of the
30 Department of Health and Human Services pursuant to NRS 425.520. The
31 statement must be completed and signed by the applicant.
32 2. The Division shall include the statement required pursuant to subsection
33 1 in:
34 (a) The application or any other forms that must be submitted for the
35 issuance or renewal of the certificate; or
36 (b) A separate form prescribed by the Division.
37 3. A certificate to operate an intermediary service organization may not be
38 issued or renewed by the Division if the applicant:
39 (a) Fails to submit the statement required pursuant to subsection 1; or
40 (b) Indicates on the statement submitted pursuant to subsection 1 that the
41 applicant is subject to a court order for the support of a child and is not in
42 compliance with the order or a plan approved by the district attorney or other
43 public agency enforcing the order for the repayment of the amount owed
44 pursuant to the order.
45 4. If an applicant indicates on the statement submitted pursuant to
46 subsection 1 that the applicant is subject to a court order for the support of a
47 child and is not in compliance with the order or a plan approved by the district
48 attorney or other public agency enforcing the order for the repayment of the
49 amount owed pursuant to the order, the Division shall advise the applicant to
50 contact the district attorney or other public agency enforcing the order to
51 determine the actions that the applicant may take to satisfy the arrearage.
52 Sec. 66. Each application for a certificate to operate an intermediary
53 service organization must be accompanied by such fee as may be determined by
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 29
1 regulation of the Board. The Board may, by regulation, allow or require payment
2 of a fee for a certificate in installments and may fix the amount of each payment
3 and the date on which the payment is due.
4 Sec. 67. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6 and section 68 of
5 this act, each intermediary service organization shall, when applying for a
6 certificate or renewing a certificate, file with the Administrator of the Division of
7 Public and Behavioral Health a surety bond:
8 (a) If the intermediary service organization employs less than 7 employees, in
9 the amount of $5,000;
10 (b) If the intermediary service organization employs at least 7 but not more
11 than 25 employees, in the amount of $25,000; or
12 (c) If the intermediary service organization employs more than 25 employees,
13 in the amount of $50,000.
14 2. A bond filed pursuant to this section must be executed by the
15 intermediary service organization as principal and by a surety company as surety.
16 The bond must be payable to the Aging and Disability Services Division of the
17 Department of Health and Human Services and must be conditioned to provide
18 indemnification to an older patient whom the Attorney for the Rights of Older
19 Persons and Persons with a Physical Disability, an Intellectual Disability or a
20 Related Condition determines has suffered property damage as a result of any act
21 or failure to act by the intermediary service organization to protect the property of
22 the older patient.
23 3. Except when a surety is released, the surety bond must cover the period
24 of the initial certificate to operate or the period of the renewal, as appropriate.
25 4. A surety on any bond filed pursuant to this section may be released after
26 the surety gives 30 days’ written notice to the Administrator of the Division of
27 Public and Behavioral Health, but the release does not discharge or otherwise
28 affect any claim filed by an older patient for property damaged as a result of any
29 act or failure to act by the intermediary service organization to protect the
30 property of the older patient alleged to have occurred while the bond was in
31 effect.
32 5. A certificate is suspended by operation of law when the intermediary
33 service organization is no longer covered by a surety bond as required by this
34 section or by a substitute for the surety bond pursuant to section 68 of this act.
35 The Administrator of the Division of Public and Behavioral Health shall give the
36 intermediary service organization at least 20 days’ written notice before the
37 release of the surety or the substitute for the surety, to the effect that the
38 certificate will be suspended by operation of law until another surety bond or
39 substitute for the surety bond is filed in the same manner and amount as the bond
40 or substitute being terminated.
41 6. The requirement of filing a surety bond set forth in this section does not
42 apply to an intermediary service organization that is operated and maintained by
43 the State of Nevada or an agency thereof.
44 7. As used in this section, “older patient” means a patient who is 60 years of
45 age or older.
46 Sec. 68. 1. As a substitute for the surety bond required pursuant to
47 section 67 of this act, an intermediary service organization may deposit with any

52 (b) Bills, bonds, notes, debentures or other obligations of the United States or
53 any agency or instrumentality thereof, or guaranteed by the United States; or
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 30
1 (c) Any obligation of this State or any city, county, town, township, school
2 district or other instrumentality of this State, or guaranteed by this State, in an
3 aggregate amount, based upon principal amount or market value, whichever is
4 lower.
5 2. The obligations of a bank, savings and loan association, savings bank,
6 thrift company or credit union must be held to secure the same obligation as
7 would the surety bond required by section 67 of this act. With the approval of the
8 Administrator of the Division of Public and Behavioral Health, the depositor may
9 substitute other suitable obligations for those deposited, which must be assigned
10 to the Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health and
11 Human Services and are negotiable only upon approval by the Administrator of
12 the Aging and Disability Services Division.
13 3. Any interest or dividends earned on the deposit accrue to the account of
14 the depositor.
15 4. The deposit must be an amount at least equal to the surety bond required
16 by section 67 of this act and must state that the amount may not be withdrawn
17 except by direct and sole order of the Administrator of the Aging and Disability
18 Services Division.

39 Sec. 70. 1. The Division shall develop and implement a process by which
40 a person with a criminal history may petition the Division to review the criminal
41 history of the person to determine if the person’s criminal history will disqualify
42 the person from obtaining a certificate to operate an intermediary service
43 organization pursuant to section 62 of this act.
44 2. Not later than 90 days after a petition is submitted to the Division
45 pursuant to subsection 1, the Division shall inform the person of the
46 determination of the Division of whether the person’s criminal history will
47 disqualify the person from obtaining a certificate. The Division is not bound by
48 its determination of disqualification or qualification and may rescind such a
49 determination at any time.
50 3. The Division may provide instructions to a person who receives a
51 determination of disqualification to remedy the determination of disqualification.
52 A person may resubmit a petition pursuant to subsection 1 not earlier than 6
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 31
1 months after receiving instructions pursuant to this subsection if the person
2 remedies the determination of disqualification.
3 4. A person with a criminal history may petition the Division at any time,
4 including, without limitation, before obtaining any education or paying any fee
5 required to obtain a certificate from the Division.
6 5. A person may submit a new petition to the Division not earlier than 2
7 years after the final determination of the initial petition submitted to the Division.
8 6. The Division may impose a fee of up to $50 upon the person to fund the
9 administrative costs in complying with the provisions of this section. The Division
10 may waive such fees or allow such fees to be covered by funds from a scholarship
11 or grant.
12 7. The Division may post on its Internet website:
13 (a) The requirements to obtain a certificate from the Division; and
14 (b) A list of crimes, if any, that would disqualify a person from obtaining a
15 certificate from the Division.
16 8. The Division may request the criminal history record of a person who

20 which includes a report from:

22 (b) The Federal Bureau of Investigation.

16 Sec. 86. 1. If an intermediary service organization violates any provision
17 related to its certification, including, without limitation, any provision of sections
18 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act or any condition, standard or regulation adopted by
19 the Board, the Division, in accordance with the regulations adopted pursuant to
20 section 87 of this act, may, as it deems appropriate:
21 (a) Prohibit the intermediary service organization from providing services
22 pursuant to section 60 of this act until it determines that the intermediary service
23 organization has corrected the violation;
24 (b) Impose an administrative penalty of not more than $1,000 per day for
25 each violation, together with interest thereon at a rate not to exceed 10 percent
26 per annum; and
27 (c) Appoint temporary management to oversee the operation of the
28 intermediary service organization and to ensure the health and safety of the
29 persons for whom the intermediary service organization performs services, until:
30 (1) It determines that the intermediary service organization has corrected
31 the violation and has management which is capable of ensuring continued
32 compliance with the applicable statutes, conditions, standards and regulations; or
33 (2) Improvements are made to correct the violation.
34 2. If the intermediary service organization fails to pay any administrative
35 penalty imposed pursuant to paragraph (b) of subsection 1, the Division may:
36 (a) Suspend the certificate to operate an intermediary service organization
37 which is held by the intermediary service organization until the administrative
38 penalty is paid; and
39 (b) Collect court costs, reasonable attorney’s fees and other costs incurred to
40 collect the administrative penalty.
41 3. The Division may require any intermediary service organization that
42 violates any provision of sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act, or any condition,
43 standard or regulation adopted by the Board, to make any improvements
44 necessary to correct the violation.
45 4. Any money collected as administrative penalties pursuant to this section
46 must be accounted for separately and used to protect the health or property of the
47 persons for whom the intermediary service organization performs services in
48 accordance with applicable federal standards.

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 49
1 NOTICE TO TENANTS OF THE PROPERTY
2
3 Foreclosure proceedings against this property have started, and a notice of
4 sale of the property to the highest bidder has been issued.
5
6 You may either: (1) terminate your lease or rental agreement and move out;
7 or (2) remain and possibly be subject to eviction proceedings under chapter
8 40 of the Nevada Revised Statutes. Any subtenants may also be subject to
9 eviction proceedings.
10
11 Between now and the date of the sale, you may be evicted if you fail to pay
12 rent or live up to your other obligations to the landlord.
13
14 After the date of the sale, you may be evicted if you fail to pay rent or live
15 up to your other obligations to the successful bidder, in accordance with
16 chapter 118A of the Nevada Revised Statutes.
17
18 Under the Nevada Revised Statutes, eviction proceedings may begin
19 against you after you have been given a notice to surrender.
20
21 If the property is sold and you pay rent by the week or another period of
22 time that is shorter than 1 month, you should generally receive notice after
23 not less than the number of days in that period of time.
24
25 If the property is sold and you pay rent by the month or any other period of
26 time that is 1 month or longer, you should generally receive notice at least
27 60 days in advance.
28
29 Under Nevada Revised Statutes 40.280, notice must generally be served on
30 you pursuant to chapter 40 of the Nevada Revised Statutes.
31
32 If the property is sold and a landlord, successful bidder or subsequent
33 purchaser files an eviction action against you in court, you will be served
34 with a summons and complaint and have the opportunity to respond.
35 Eviction actions may result in temporary evictions, permanent evictions, the
36 awarding of damages pursuant to Nevada Revised Statutes 40.360 or some
37 combination of those results.
38
39 Under the Justice Court Rules of Civil Procedure:
40 (1) You will be given at least 10 days to answer a summons and
41 complaint;
42 (2) If you do not file an answer, an order evicting you by default may
43 be obtained against you;
44 (3) A hearing regarding a temporary eviction may be called as soon as
45 11 days after you are served with the summons and complaint; and
46 (4) A hearing regarding a permanent eviction may be called as soon as

7 Sec. 109. NRS 118A.335 is hereby amended to read as follows:
8 118A.335 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6, a landlord of
9 dwelling units intended and operated exclusively for persons 55 years of age and
10 older may not employ any person who will work 36 hours or more per week and
11 who will have access to all dwelling units to perform work on the premises unless
12 the person has obtained a work card issued pursuant to subsection 2 by the sheriff
13 of the county in which the dwelling units are located and renewed that work card as
14 necessary.
15 2. The sheriff of a county shall issue a work card to each person who is
16 required by this section to obtain a work card and who complies with the
17 requirements established by the sheriff for the issuance of such a card. A work card
18 issued pursuant to this section must be renewed:
19 (a) Every 5 years; and
20 (b) Whenever the person changes his or her employment to perform work for
21 an employer other than the employer for which the person’s current work card was
22 issued.
23 3. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 4, if the sheriff of a county
24 requires an applicant for a work card to be investigated:
25 (a) The applicant must submit with his or her application a complete set of his
26 or her fingerprints and written permission authorizing the sheriff to forward the
27 fingerprints to the Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History for
28 submission to the Federal Bureau of Investigation for its report.
29 (b) The sheriff shall submit the fingerprints to the Central Repository for
30 Nevada Records of Criminal History for submission to the Federal Bureau of
31 Investigation to determine the criminal history of the applicant.
32 (c) The sheriff may issue a temporary work card pending the determination of
33 the criminal history of the applicant by the Federal Bureau of Investigation.
34 4. The sheriff of a county shall not require an investigation of the criminal
35 history of an employee or independent contractor of an agency , [or] facility or
36 organization governed by NRS 449.122 to 449.125, inclusive, and 449.174 ,
37 sections 36 to 40, inclusive, and section 49 of this act, or sections 80 to 85,
38 inclusive, of this act, as applicable, who has had his or her fingerprints submitted
39 to the Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History pursuant to NRS
40 449.123 or section 37 or 81 of this act, as applicable, for an investigation of his or
41 her criminal history within the immediately preceding 6 months.
42 5. The sheriff shall not issue a work card to any person who:
43 (a) Has been convicted of a category A, B or C felony or of a crime in another
44 state which would be a category A, B or C felony if committed in this State;
45 (b) Has been convicted of a sexual offense;
46 (c) Has been convicted of a crime against any person who is 60 years of age or
47 older or against a vulnerable person for which an additional term of imprisonment
48 may be imposed pursuant to NRS 193.167 or the laws of any other jurisdiction;
49 (d) Has been convicted of a battery punishable as a gross misdemeanor; or
50 (e) Within the immediately preceding 5 years:
51 (1) Has been convicted of a theft; or
52 (2) Has been convicted of a violation of any state or federal law regulating
53 the possession, distribution or use of a controlled substance.

9 Sec. 113. NRS 200.5093 is hereby amended to read as follows:

23 710.159, 711.600, and sections 23, 55 and 69 of this act, sections 35, 38 and 41 of
24 chapter 478, Statutes of Nevada 2011 and section 2 of chapter 391, Statutes of
25 Nevada 2013 and unless otherwise declared by law to be confidential, all public
26 books and public records of a governmental entity must be open at all times during
27 office hours to inspection by any person, and may be fully copied or an abstract or
28 memorandum may be prepared from those public books and public records. Any
29 such copies, abstracts or memoranda may be used to supply the general public with
30 copies, abstracts or memoranda of the records or may be used in any other way to
31 the advantage of the governmental entity or of the general public. This section does
32 not supersede or in any manner affect the federal laws governing copyrights or
33 enlarge, diminish or affect in any other manner the rights of a person in any written
34 book or record which is copyrighted pursuant to federal law.
35 2. A governmental entity may not reject a book or record which is
36 copyrighted solely because it is copyrighted.
37 3. A governmental entity that has legal custody or control of a public book or
38 record shall not deny a request made pursuant to subsection 1 to inspect or copy or
39 receive a copy of a public book or record on the basis that the requested public
40 book or record contains information that is confidential if the governmental entity
41 can redact, delete, conceal or separate, including, without limitation, electronically,
42 the confidential information from the information included in the public book or
43 record that is not otherwise confidential.
44 4. If requested, a governmental entity shall provide a copy of a public record
45 in an electronic format by means of an electronic medium. Nothing in this
46 subsection requires a governmental entity to provide a copy of a public record in an
47 electronic format or by means of an electronic medium if:
48 (a) The public record:
49 (1) Was not created or prepared in an electronic format; and
50 (2) Is not available in an electronic format; or
51 (b) Providing the public record in an electronic format or by means of an
52 electronic medium would:
53 (1) Give access to proprietary software; or
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 68
1 (2) Require the production of information that is confidential and that
2 cannot be redacted, deleted, concealed or separated from information that is not
3 otherwise confidential.
4 5. An officer, employee or agent of a governmental entity who has legal
5 custody or control of a public record:
6 (a) Shall not refuse to provide a copy of that public record in the medium that
7 is requested because the officer, employee or agent has already prepared or would
8 prefer to provide the copy in a different medium.
9 (b) Except as otherwise provided in NRS 239.030, shall, upon request, prepare
10 the copy of the public record and shall not require the person who has requested the
11 copy to prepare the copy himself or herself.

42 persons who are more than 60 years of age to receive, as a portion of their
43 continuing education, education in geriatrics and gerontology, including such topics
44 as:
45 (a) The skills and knowledge that the licensee needs to address aging issues;
46 (b) Approaches to providing health care to older persons, including both
47 didactic and clinical approaches;
48 (c) The biological, behavioral, social and emotional aspects of the aging
49 process; and
50 (d) The importance of maintenance of function and independence for older
51 persons.
52 5. The Board shall encourage each holder of a license to practice medicine to
53 receive, as a portion of his or her continuing education, training concerning
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 75
1 methods for educating patients about how to effectively manage medications,
2 including, without limitation, the ability of the patient to request to have the
3 symptom or purpose for which a drug is prescribed included on the label attached to
4 the container of the drug.
5 6. The Board shall require each holder of a license to practice medicine to
6 receive as a portion of his or her continuing education at least 2 hours of instruction
7 every 4 years on evidence-based suicide prevention and awareness, which may
8 include, without limitation, instruction concerning:
9 (a) The skills and knowledge that the licensee needs to detect behaviors that
10 may lead to suicide, including, without limitation, post-traumatic stress disorder;
11 (b) Approaches to engaging other professionals in suicide intervention; and
12 (c) The detection of suicidal thoughts and ideations and the prevention of
13 suicide.
14 7. The Board shall encourage each holder of a license to practice medicine or
15 as a physician assistant to receive, as a portion of his or her continuing education,
16 training and education in the diagnosis of rare diseases, including, without
17 limitation:
18 (a) Recognizing the symptoms of pediatric cancer; and
19 (b) Interpreting family history to determine whether such symptoms indicate a
20 normal childhood illness or a condition that requires additional examination.
21 8. A holder of a license to practice medicine may not substitute the continuing
22 education credits relating to suicide prevention and awareness required by this
23 section for the purposes of satisfying an equivalent requirement for continuing
24 education in ethics.
25 9. Except as otherwise provided in NRS 630.2535, a holder of a license to
26 practice medicine may substitute not more than 2 hours of continuing education
27 credits in pain management, care for persons with an addictive disorder or the
28 screening, brief intervention and referral to treatment approach to substance use
29 disorder for the purposes of satisfying an equivalent requirement for continuing
30 education in ethics.

32 (a) “Act of terrorism” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 202.4415.
33 (b) “Biological agent” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 202.442.
34 (c) “Chemical agent” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS 202.4425.

18 (b) A requirement that the applicant receive at least 3 hours of instruction
19 relating to cultural competency and diversity, equity and inclusion for each year of
20 the term of the applicant’s licensure or certification. Such instruction:
21 (1) May include the training provided pursuant to NRS 449.103 [,] or
22 section 34 of this act, where applicable.
23 (2) Must be based upon a range of research from diverse sources.
24 (3) Must address persons of different cultural backgrounds, including,
25 without limitation:
26 (I) Persons from various gender, racial and ethnic backgrounds;
27 (II) Persons from various religious backgrounds;
28 (III) Lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender and questioning persons;
29 (IV) Children and senior citizens;
30 (V) Veterans;
31 (VI) Persons with a mental illness;
32 (VII) Persons with an intellectual disability, developmental disability
33 or physical disability; and
34 (VIII) Persons who are part of any other population that the holder of a
35 license or certificate may need to better understand, as determined by the Board.
36 4. If the applicant is a certified intern, the name of the licensed or certified
37 counselor who supervises the applicant.
38 5. All information required to complete the renewal.
39 Sec. 145. NRS 641D.360 is hereby amended to read as follows:
40 641D.360 1. To renew a license as a behavior analyst or assistant behavior
41 analyst or registration as a registered behavior technician, each person must, on or
42 before the first day of January of each odd-numbered year:
43 (a) Apply to the Board for renewal;
44 (b) Pay the biennial fee for the renewal of a license or registration;
45 (c) Submit evidence to the Board:
46 (1) Of completion of the requirements for continuing education as set forth
47 in regulations adopted by the Board, if applicable; and
48 (2) That the person’s certification or registration, as applicable, by the
49 Behavior Analyst Certification Board, Inc., or its successor organization, remains
50 valid and the holder remains in good standing; and
51 (d) Submit all information required to complete the renewal.
52 2. In addition to the requirements of subsection 1, to renew registration as a
53 registered behavior technician for the third time and every third renewal thereafter,
Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 85
1 a person must submit to an investigation of his or her criminal history in the manner
2 prescribed in paragraph (b) of subsection 1 of NRS 641D.300.
3 3. The Board shall adopt regulations that require, as a prerequisite for the
4 renewal of a license as a behavior analyst or assistant behavior analyst, each holder
5 to complete continuing education, which must:
6 (a) Be consistent with nationally recognized standards for the continuing
7 education of behavior analysts or assistant behavior analysts, as applicable.
8 (b) Include, without limitation, a requirement that the holder of a license
9 receive at least 2 hours of instruction on evidence-based suicide prevention and
10 awareness.
11 (c) Include, without limitation, a requirement that the holder of a license as a
12 behavior analyst receive at least 6 hours of instruction relating to cultural
13 competency and diversity, equity and inclusion. Such instruction:
14 (1) May include the training provided pursuant to NRS 449.103 [,] or
15 section 34 of this act, where applicable.
16 (2) Must be based upon a range of research from diverse sources.
17 (3) Must address persons of different cultural backgrounds, including,
18 without limitation:
19 (I) Persons from various gender, racial and ethnic backgrounds;
20 (II) Persons from various religious backgrounds;
21 (III) Lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender and questioning persons;
22 (IV) Children and senior citizens;
23 (V) Veterans;
24 (VI) Persons with a mental illness;
25 (VII) Persons with an intellectual disability, developmental disability
26 or physical disability; and
27 (VIII) Persons who are part of any other population that a behavior
28 analyst may need to better understand, as determined by the Board.
29 4. The Board shall not adopt regulations requiring a registered behavior
30 technician to receive continuing education.

10 Sec. 148. 1. A license to operate an agency to provide personal care

DAN/EWR Date: 4/19/2025
A.B. No. 519—Creates a separate chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes
governing certain agencies and organizations that provide
nonmedical services. (BDR 40-805)
*A_AB519_451*
Page 1 of 88

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 3
ASSEMBLY BILL NO. 519–COMMITTEE ON
HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES
MARCH 24, 2025
_______________
Referred to Committee on Health and Human Services
SUMMARY—Creates a separate chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes governing
certain agencies and organizations that provide nonmedical
services. (BDR 40-805)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: No.
Effect on the State: Yes.
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to health care; establishing separate provisions for the licensing
or certification, regulation and discipline of agencies to provide
personal care services in the home, employment agencies that contract
to provide certain nonmedical services and intermediary service
organizations; enacting provisions to facilitate the collecting of certain
debts from applicants for certain licenses; imposing certain
requirements as an applicant for a certificate to operate an intermediary
service organization; revising the training requirements for certain
caregivers who receive reimbursement through Medicaid;
authorizing a family member to serve as the personal care
assistant for a recipient of Medicaid under certain circumstances;
providing penalties; and providing other matters properly relating
thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 Existing law provides for the licensure and regulation of various types of medical
2 facilities and facilities for the dependent by the Division of Public and Behavioral Health of
3 the Department of Health and Human Services. (Chapter 449 of NRS) Existing law requires
4 an agency to provide personal care services in the home to be licensed by the Division as a
5 facility for the dependent. (NRS 449.0045, 449.030) Existing law requires an employment
6 agency that contracts with persons in this State to provide nonmedical services related to
7 personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home to obtain a license
8 from the State Board of Health. (NRS 449.03005) Existing law requires an intermediary
9 service organization to obtain a certificate from the Division. (NRS 449.431) Existing law
10 requires the Board to adopt regulations governing agencies to provide personal care services
11 in the home, employment agencies that contract to provide nonmedical services related to
12 personal care to elderly persons and persons with disabilities and intermediary service
13 organizations. (NRS 449.03005, 449.0302, 449.4309)
14 This bill transfers the provisions of law governing agencies to provide personal care
15 services in the home, employment agencies that contract to provide nonmedical services
16 related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home and

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 4
17 intermediary service organizations from the chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes that
18 generally governs medical facilities and facilities for the dependent to a new chapter in the
19 Nevada Revised Statutes without changing the current substantive provisions that govern such
20 agencies and organizations. Sections 2-19, 24-49, 51-60, 69-79 and 81-90 of this bill create a
21 new chapter consisting of provisions for the licensure and regulation of such entities in a
22 manner substantially identical to the manner in which those entities are licensed and
23 regulated under existing law. Sections 94, 96-104 and 150 of this bill eliminate provisions
24 governing those entities from the chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes that regulates
25 medical facilities and facilities for the dependent. Sections 93, 111, 113, 117, 118, 120-123,
26 126-133, 138 and 146 of this bill eliminate references to sections repealed by section 150.
27 Sections 91, 92, 95 and 105-146 of this bill make various conforming changes so that the
28 legal status of agencies to provide personal care services in the home, employment agencies
29 that contract to provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or
30 persons with disabilities in the home and intermediary service organizations is not changed by
31 this bill.
32 Existing federal law requires each state to adopt procedures to ensure that applicants for
33 certain licenses and certificates comply with child support obligations, including by requiring
34 an applicant for such a license to provide his or her social security number. (42 U.S.C. § 666)
35 Sections 20, 21 and 50 of this bill enact such procedures as applicable to an applicant for the
36 issuance or renewal of a license to operate an agency to provide personal care services in the
37 home or an employment agency that contracts to provide nonmedical services related to
38 personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home in order to comply
39 with federal law. Section 23 of this bill establishes alternate provisions for such an applicant
40 who does not have a social security number. Section 22 of this bill also requires an applicant
41 for the renewal of such a license to provide certain information for the purpose of identifying
42 persons who owe certain debts to the State. Sections 65, 69, 74 and 76 of this bill establish
43 similar provisions for intermediary service organizations, which were carried over from
44 existing law. (NRS 449.4312, 449.4313, 449.4315, 449.432, 449.4322)
45 Existing law requires: (1) an agency to provide personal care services in the home to file
46 with the Administrator of the Division a surety bond or a substitute for a surety bond; and (2)
47 an applicant for a license to operate an agency to provide personal care services in the home to
48 undergo a criminal background check. (NRS 449.065, 449.067, 449.122) Sections 67, 68 and
49 80 of this bill impose similar requirements on intermediary service organizations.
50 Existing law requires: (1) the Department to apply for a home and community-
51 based services waiver to include structured family caregiving for certain persons as
52 medical assistance under Medicaid; and (2) a caregiver providing care under that waiver
53 to complete training required by the Aging and Disability Services Division of the
54 Department. (NRS 422.3965) Sections 30 and 122 of this bill instead require such a
55 caregiver to complete the same training that is required for unlicensed caregivers who
56 provide care for an agency to provide personal care services in the home.
57 Existing law requires the Director of the Department to include in the State Plan for
58 Medicaid authorization for a recipient of Medicaid to be deemed a provider of services
59 for the purposes of allowing the recipient to receive reimbursement for personal care
60 services covered by Medicaid and using that money to pay for services provided by a
61 personal care assistant or an agency to provide personal care services in the home. (NRS
62 422.272407). Section 120 of this bill authorizes a family member of a recipient of
63 Medicaid to serve as a personal care assistant for a recipient of Medicaid if the family
64 member: (1) completes the training required by section 30 for certain other caregivers;
65 and (2) receives authorization from a provider of health care.
66 Section 147 of this bill requires the Legislative Counsel to move regulations specifically
67 relating to such entities to a new chapter of the Nevada Administrative Code that corresponds
68 to the new chapter of the Nevada Revised Statutes created by sections 2-90. Section 147 also:
69 (1) requires the Board to adopt new regulations to replace other regulations relating to those
70 entities that remain in the chapter of the Nevada Administrative Code governing medical
71 facilities and facilities for the dependent; and (2) provides that those existing regulations
72 remain in effect until the Board adopts new regulations to replace them. Section 148 of this
73 bill clarifies that this bill does not affect the validity of: (1) licenses or certificates to operate
74 agencies to provide personal care services in the home, employment agencies that contract to
75 provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 5
76 disabilities in the home and intermediary service organizations; (2) certain training completed
77 by the operators, employees and contractors of such entities; or (3) disciplinary actions taken
78 against such entities.
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:
1 Section 1. Title 40 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto a new
2 chapter to consist of the provisions set forth as sections 2 to 90, inclusive, of this
3 act.
4 Sec. 2. As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires, the
5 words and terms defined in sections 3 to 7, inclusive, of this act have the
6 meanings ascribed to them in those sections.
7 Sec. 3. 1. “Agency to provide personal care services in the home” means
8 any person, other than a natural person, which provides services authorized
9 pursuant to section 52 of this act to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in
10 the home.
11 2. The term does not include:
12 (a) An independent contractor who provides nonmedical services specified in
13 section 52 of this act without the assistance of employees;
14 (b) An organized group of persons composed of the family and friends of a
15 person needing nonmedical services related to personal care that employs or
16 contracts with persons to provide such nonmedical services for the person if:
17 (1) The organization of the group of persons is set forth in a written
18 document that is made available for review by the Division upon request; and
19 (2) The services are provided to only one person or one family who
20 resides in the same residence;
21 (c) An intermediary service organization; or
22 (d) A person or agency that contracts with the Aging and Disability Services
23 Division of the Department of Health and Human Services to provide temporary
24 respite services.
25 3. As used in this section:
26 (a) “Intermediary service organization” has the meaning ascribed to it in
27 section 59 of this act.
28 (b) “Temporary respite services” means services provided through a contract
29 with the Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health and
30 Human Services to a natural person on a periodic basis to provide a respite for a
31 regular provider of services.
32 Sec. 4. “Board” means the State Board of Health.
33 Sec. 5. “Division” means the Division of Public and Behavioral Health of
34 the Department of Health and Human Services.
35 Sec. 6. “Employment agency” has the meaning ascribed to it in NRS
36 611.020.
37 Sec. 7. “Nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or
38 persons with disabilities” includes, without limitation:
39 1. The elimination of wastes from the body;
40 2. Dressing and undressing;
41 3. Bathing;
42 4. Grooming;
43 5. The preparation and eating of meals;
44 6. Laundry;

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 6
1 7. Shopping;
2 8. Cleaning;
3 9. Transportation; and
4 10. Any other minor needs related to the maintenance of personal hygiene.
5 Sec. 8. Except as otherwise provided in section 12 of this act, no person,
6 state or local government or agency thereof may operate or maintain in this State
7 an agency to provide personal care services in the home without first obtaining a
8 license as provided in sections 8 to 58, inclusive, of this act.
9 Sec. 9. 1. Except as otherwise provided in section 12 of this act, a person
10 must obtain a license from the Board to operate an employment agency that
11 contracts with persons in this State to provide nonmedical services related to
12 personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in the home,
13 regardless of whether the employment agency is located in this State.
14 2. The Board shall adopt:
15 (a) Standards for licensing of employment agencies that contract to provide
16 nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with
17 disabilities in the home;
18 (b) Standards relating to the fees charged by such employment agencies;
19 (c) Regulations governing the licensing of such employment agencies; and
20 (d) Regulations establishing requirements for training the persons who
21 contract with such employment agencies to provide such nonmedical services.
22 3. An employment agency that is licensed pursuant to this section shall not
23 refer a person to a home to provide nonmedical services related to personal care
24 to elderly persons or persons with disabilities if that person has not met the
25 requirements set forth in sections 36 to 40, inclusive, of this act.
26 4. A person who violates the provisions of subsection 3 is liable for a civil
27 penalty to be recovered by the Attorney General in the name of the Board for the
28 first offense of not more than $10,000 and for a second and subsequent offense
29 of not less than $10,000 nor more than $20,000. Unless otherwise required by
30 federal law, the Board shall deposit all civil penalties collected pursuant to this
31 section into a separate account in the State General Fund to be used to
32 administer and carry out the provisions of chapter 449A of NRS and sections 2 to
33 58, inclusive, of this act and to protect the health, safety, well-being and property
34 of the persons served by the employment agencies.
35 Sec. 10. 1. The Division shall develop and implement a process by which
36 a person with a criminal history may petition the Division to review the criminal
37 history of the person to determine if the person’s criminal history will disqualify
38 the person from obtaining a license pursuant to sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this
39 act.
40 2. Not later than 90 days after a petition is submitted to the Division
41 pursuant to subsection 1, the Division shall inform the person of the
42 determination of the Division of whether the person’s criminal history will
43 disqualify the person from obtaining a license. The Division is not bound by its
44 determination of disqualification or qualification and may rescind such a
45 determination at any time.
46 3. The Division may provide instructions to a person who receives a
47 determination of disqualification to remedy the determination of disqualification.
48 A person may resubmit a petition pursuant to subsection 1 not earlier than 6
49 months after receiving instructions pursuant to this subsection if the person
50 remedies the determination of disqualification.
51 4. A person with a criminal history may petition the Division at any time,
52 including, without limitation, before obtaining any education or paying any fee
53 required to obtain a license from the Division.

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 7
1 5. A person may submit a new petition to the Division not earlier than 2
2 years after the final determination of the initial petition submitted to the Division.
3 6. The Division may impose a fee of up to $50 upon the person to fund the
4 administrative costs in complying with the provisions of this section. The Division
5 may waive such fees or allow such fees to be covered by funds from a scholarship
6 or grant.
7 7. The Division may post on its Internet website:

34 Sec. 11. The provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act do not
35 apply to any agency to provide personal care services in the home that is operated

42 Sec. 13. 1. The Board shall adopt:
43 (a) Licensing standards for agencies to provide personal care services in the

45 (b) Regulations governing the licensing of such agencies.

1 Sec. 14. 1. The Board shall adopt regulations authorizing an employee of
2 an agency to provide personal care services in the home, with the consent of the
3 person receiving services, to:
4 (a) Check, record and report the temperature, blood pressure, apical or
5 radial pulse, respiration or oxygen saturation of a person receiving services from
6 the agency;
7 (b) Using an auto-injection device approved by the Food and Drug
8 Administration for use in the home, administer to a person receiving services
9 from the agency insulin furnished by a registered pharmacist, as directed by a
10 physician, physician assistant or advanced practice registered nurse, or assist
11 such a person with the self-administration of such insulin; and
12 (c) Using a device for monitoring blood glucose approved by the Food and
13 Drug Administration for use in the home, conduct a blood glucose test on a
14 person receiving services from the agency or assist such a person to conduct a
15 blood glucose test on himself or herself.
16 2. The regulations adopted pursuant to this section:
17 (a) Must require the tasks described in subsection 1 to be performed in
18 conformance with the Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments of 1988,
19 Public Law No. 100-578, 42 U.S.C. § 263a, if applicable, and any other
20 applicable federal law or regulation;
21 (b) Must prohibit the use of a device for monitoring blood glucose on more
22 than one person; and
23 (c) May require a person to receive training before performing any task
24 described in subsection 1.

47 Sec. 24. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6 and section 25 of

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 11
1 (c) If the agency employs more than 25 employees, in the amount of $50,000.
2 2. A bond filed pursuant to this section must be executed by the agency as
3 principal and by a surety company as surety. The bond must be payable to the
4 Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health and Human
5 Services and must be conditioned to provide indemnification to an older client
6 who the Attorney for the Rights of Older Persons and Persons with a Physical
7 Disability, an Intellectual Disability or a Related Condition determines has
8 suffered property damage as a result of any act or failure to act by the agency to
9 protect the property of the older client.
10 3. Except when a surety is released, the surety bond must cover the period
11 of the initial license to operate or the period of the renewal, as appropriate.
12 4. A surety on any bond filed pursuant to this section may be released after
13 the surety gives 30 days’ written notice to the Administrator of the Division of
14 Public and Behavioral Health, but the release does not discharge or otherwise
15 affect any claim filed by an older client for property damaged as a result of any
16 act or failure to act by the agency to protect the property of the older client
17 alleged to have occurred while the bond was in effect.
18 5. A license is suspended by operation of law when the agency is no longer
19 covered by a surety bond as required by this section or by a substitute for the
20 surety bond pursuant to section 25 of this act. The Administrator of the Division
21 of Public and Behavioral Health shall give the agency at least 20 days’ written
22 notice before the release of the surety or the substitute for the surety, to the effect
23 that the license will be suspended by operation of law until another surety bond
24 or substitute for the surety bond is filed in the same manner and amount as the
25 bond or substitute being terminated.
26 6. The requirement of filing a surety bond set forth in this section does not

32 Sec. 31. 1. An applicant for a license to operate an agency to provide
33 personal care services in the home must receive training to recognize and prevent
34 the abuse of older persons before a license to operate such an agency is issued to
35 the applicant. If an applicant has completed such training within the year
36 preceding the date of the application for a license and the application includes
37 evidence of the training, the applicant shall be deemed to have complied with the
38 requirements of this subsection.
39 2. A licensee who holds a license to operate an agency to provide personal
40 care services in the home must annually receive training to recognize and prevent
41 the abuse of older persons before the license to operate such an agency may be
42 renewed.
43 3. If an applicant or licensee who is required by this section to obtain
44 training is not a natural person, the person in charge of the agency must receive
45 the training required by this section.
46 4. An administrator or other person in charge of an agency to provide
47 personal care services in the home must receive training to recognize and prevent
48 the abuse of older persons before the agency provides care to a person and
49 annually thereafter.
50 5. An employee who will provide care for an agency to provide personal
51 care services in the home must receive training to recognize and prevent the
52 abuse of older persons before the employee provides care to a person in the
53 agency and annually thereafter.

18 Sec. 32. 1. An agency to provide personal care services in the home and
19 any employee or independent contractor of such an agency shall not discriminate
20 in the provision of services to a client based wholly or partially on the actual or
21 perceived race, color, religion, national origin, ancestry, age, gender, physical or
22 mental disability, sexual orientation, gender identity or expression or human
23 immunodeficiency virus status of the client or any person with whom the client
24 associates.
25 2. An agency to provide personal care services in the home shall:
26 (a) Develop and carry out policies to prevent the specific types of prohibited
27 discrimination described in the regulations adopted by the Board pursuant to
28 section 13 of this act and meet any other requirements prescribed by regulations
29 of the Board; and
30 (b) Post prominently on any Internet website used to market the agency the
31 following statement:
32
33 [Name of the agency to provide personal care services in the home] does
34 not discriminate and does not permit discrimination, including, without
35 limitation, bullying, abuse or harassment, on the basis of actual or
36 perceived race, color, religion, national origin, ancestry, age, gender,
37 physical or mental disability, sexual orientation, gender identity or
38 expression or HIV status, or based on association with another person on
39 account of that person’s actual or perceived race, color, religion, national
40 origin, ancestry, age, gender, physical or mental disability, sexual
41 orientation, gender identity or expression or HIV status.

43 3. The provisions of this section shall not be construed to:
44 (a) Require an agency to provide personal care services in the home or an
45 employee or independent contractor thereof to take or refrain from taking any
46 action in violation of reasonable medical standards; or
47 (b) Prohibit an agency to provide personal care services in the home from
48 adopting a policy that is applied uniformly and in a nondiscriminatory manner,
49 including, without limitation, such a policy that bans or restricts sexual relations.
50 Sec. 33. An agency to provide personal care services in the home shall:
51 1. Maintain the confidentiality of personally identifiable information
52 concerning the sexual orientation of a client, whether the client is transgender or
53 has undergone gender-affirming surgery and the human immunodeficiency virus

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 15
1 status of the client and take reasonable actions to prevent the unauthorized
2 disclosure of such information;
3 2. Prohibit employees or independent contractors of the agency who are not
4 directly providing care to a client from being present during any portion of the
5 care, during which the client is fully or partially unclothed without the express
6 permission of the client or the authorized representative of the client;
7 3. Use visual barriers, including, without limitation, doors, curtains and
8 screens, to provide privacy for clients who are fully or partially unclothed; and
9 4. Allow a client to refuse to be examined or observed by or receive services
10 from an employee or independent contractor of the agency for a purpose that is
11 primarily educational rather than therapeutic.
12 Sec. 34. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, to enable an

31 2. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, the requirements of

14 with the person’s training, in the course of his or her regular employment or
15 profession, to an elderly person or a person with a disability, is not liable for any
16 civil damages as a result of any act or omission, not amounting to gross
17 negligence, by that person in rendering that care.
18 Sec. 54. The name, sign, listing or other designation of an agency to
19 provide personal care services in the home must not contain any terms
20 misleading to the public with regard to the services offered.
21 Sec. 55. 1. An agency to provide personal care services in the home or an
22 employee of such an agency shall not:
23 (a) Refer a person to a residential facility for groups that is not licensed by
24 the Division; or
25 (b) Refer a person to a residential facility for groups if the agency to provide
26 personal care services in the home or its employee knows or reasonably should
27 know that the residential facility for groups, or the services provided by the
28 residential facility for groups, are not appropriate for the condition of the person
29 being referred.
30 2. If an agency to provide personal care services in the home or an
31 employee of such an agency violates the provisions of subsection 1, the agency to
32 provide personal care services in the home is liable for a civil penalty to be
33 recovered by the Attorney General in the name of the Board for the first offense
34 of not more than $10,000 and for a second or subsequent offense of not less than
35 $10,000 or more than $20,000. Unless otherwise required by federal law, the
36 Board shall deposit all civil penalties collected pursuant to this section into a
37 separate account in the State General Fund to be used for the enforcement of this
38 section and the protection of the health, safety, well-being and property of
39 residents of residential facilities for groups.
40 3. The Board shall:
41 (a) Establish and maintain a system to track violations of this section. Except
42 as otherwise provided in this paragraph, records created by or for the system are
43 public records and are available for public inspection. The following information
44 is confidential:
45 (1) Any personally identifying information relating to a person who is
46 referred to a residential facility for groups.
47 (2) Information which may not be disclosed under federal law.
48 (b) Educate the public regarding the requirements and prohibitions set forth
49 in this section and NRS 449.0305.
50 4. As used in this section, “residential facility for groups” has the meaning
51 ascribed to it in NRS 449.017.
52 Sec. 56. 1. In addition to the payment of the amount required by section
53 17 of this act and any civil penalty imposed pursuant to subsection 4, a person

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 26
1 who operates an agency to provide personal care services in the home without a
2 license issued by the Division is guilty of a misdemeanor.
3 2. If the Division believes that a person is operating an agency to provide
4 personal care services in the home without such a license, the Division may issue
5 an order to cease and desist the operation of the agency. The order must be
6 served upon the person by personal delivery or by certified or registered mail,
7 return receipt requested. The order is effective upon service.
8 3. If a person does not voluntarily cease operating an agency to provide
9 personal care services in the home without a license or apply for licensure within
10 30 days after the date of service of the order pursuant to subsection 2, the
11 Division may bring an action in a court of competent jurisdiction pursuant to
12 section 57 of this act.
13 4. Upon a showing by the Division that a person is operating an agency to
14 provide personal care services in the home without a license, a court of competent
15 jurisdiction may:
16 (a) Enjoin the person from operating the agency.
17 (b) Impose a civil penalty on the operator to be recovered by the Division of
18 not more than $10,000 for the first offense or not less than $10,000 or more than
19 $25,000 for a second or subsequent offense.
20 5. Unless otherwise required by federal law, the Division shall deposit all
21 civil penalties collected pursuant to paragraph (b) of subsection 4 into a separate
22 account in the State General Fund to be used to administer and carry out the
23 provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act and to protect the health,
24 safety, well-being and property of the clients in accordance with applicable state
25 and federal standards.
26 Sec. 57. 1. The Division may bring an action in the name of the State to
27 enjoin any person, state or local government unit or agency thereof from
28 operating or maintaining any agency to provide personal care services in the
29 home or employment agency that contracts with persons to provide nonmedical
30 services related to personal care to elderly persons or persons with disabilities in
31 the home within the meaning of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act:
32 (a) Without first obtaining a license therefor; or
33 (b) After his or her license has been revoked or suspended by the Division.
34 2. It is sufficient in such action to allege that the defendant did, on a certain
35 date and in a certain place, operate and maintain such an agency without a
36 license.
37 Sec. 58. The district attorney of the county in which an agency to provide
38 personal care services in the home or employment agency that contracts with
39 persons to provide nonmedical services related to personal care to elderly persons
40 or persons with disabilities in the home is located shall, upon application by the
41 Division, institute and conduct the prosecution of any action for violation of any
42 provisions of sections 2 to 58, inclusive, of this act.
43 Sec. 59. As used in sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act, unless the
44 context otherwise requires, “intermediary service organization” means a
45 nongovernmental entity that provides services authorized pursuant to section 60
46 of this act for a person with a disability or other responsible person.
47 Sec. 60. 1. An intermediary service organization that is certified pursuant
48 to sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act may provide services for a person with a
49 disability or other responsible person relating to personal assistance received by
50 the person with a disability. The services that may be provided by an intermediary
51 service organization include, without limitation:

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 27
1 (a) Obtaining a criminal background check of a personal assistant selected
2 by the person with a disability or other responsible person to provide nonmedical
3 services and any medical services authorized pursuant to NRS 629.091;
4 (b) Providing payroll services to pay the personal assistant and determine
5 any tax liability;
6 (c) Providing services relating to financial management; and
7 (d) Providing any other services relating to the employment of a personal
8 assistant and any other financial assistance relating to the personal assistance for
9 the person with a disability.
10 2. As used in this section:
11 (a) “Other responsible person” means:
12 (1) A parent or guardian of, or any other person legally responsible for, a
13 person with a disability who is under the age of 18 years; or
14 (2) A parent, spouse, guardian or adult child of a person with a disability
15 who suffers from a cognitive impairment.
16 (b) “Personal assistance” means the provision of any goods or services to
17 help a person with a disability maintain his or her independence, personal
18 hygiene and safety, including, without limitation, the provision of services by a
19 personal assistant.
20 (c) “Personal assistant” means a person who, for compensation and under
21 the direction of a person with a disability or other responsible person, performs
22 services for a person with a disability to help the person maintain his or her
23 independence, personal hygiene and safety.
24 Sec. 61. 1. The Board shall adopt regulations authorizing an employee of
25 an intermediary service organization, with the consent of the person receiving
26 services, to:
27 (a) Check, record and report the temperature, blood pressure, apical or
28 radial pulse, respiration or oxygen saturation of a person receiving services from
29 the organization;
30 (b) Using an auto-injection device approved by the Food and Drug
31 Administration for use in the home, administer to a person receiving services
32 from the organization insulin furnished by a registered pharmacist as directed by
33 a physician or assist such a person with the self-administration of such insulin;
34 and
35 (c) Using a device for monitoring blood glucose approved by the Food and
36 Drug Administration for use in the home, perform a blood glucose test on a
37 person receiving services from the organization or assist such a person to
38 perform a blood glucose test on himself or herself.
39 2. The regulations adopted pursuant to this section:
40 (a) Must require the tasks described in subsection 1 to be performed in
41 conformance with the Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments of 1988,
42 Public Law No. 100-578, 42 U.S.C. § 263a, if applicable, and any other
43 applicable federal law or regulation;
44 (b) Must prohibit the use of a device for monitoring blood glucose on more
45 than one person; and
46 (c) May require a person to receive training before performing any task
47 described in subsection 1.
48 Sec. 62. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, a person shall
49 not operate or maintain in this State an intermediary service organization without
50 first obtaining a certificate to operate an intermediary service organization as
51 provided in sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act.
52 2. A person who is licensed to operate an agency to provide personal care
53 services in the home pursuant to this chapter is not required to obtain a

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 28
1 certificate to operate an intermediary service organization as described in this
2 section.
3 3. A person who violates the provisions of this section is guilty of a
4 misdemeanor.
5 Sec. 63. Any person wishing to obtain a certificate to operate an
6 intermediary service organization pursuant to the provisions of sections 59 to 90,
7 inclusive, of this act must file with the Division an application, on a form
8 prescribed, prepared and furnished by the Division, containing:
9 1. The name of the applicant and, if a person, whether the applicant has
10 attained the age of 21 years.
11 2. The location of the intermediary service organization.
12 3. The name of the person in charge of the intermediary service
13 organization.
14 4. Such other information as may be required by the Division for the proper
15 administration and enforcement of sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act.
16 5. Evidence satisfactory to the Division that the applicant is of reputable
17 and responsible character. If the applicant is a firm, association, organization,
18 partnership, business trust, corporation or company, similar evidence must be
19 submitted as to the members thereof, and the person in charge of the
20 intermediary service organization for which the application is made.
21 6. Evidence satisfactory to the Division of the ability of the applicant to
22 comply with the provisions of sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act and the
23 standards and regulations adopted by the Board.
24 Sec. 64. An application for the issuance of a certificate to operate an
25 intermediary service organization pursuant to section 63 of this act must include
26 the social security number of the applicant.
27 Sec. 65. 1. An applicant for the issuance or renewal of a certificate to
28 operate an intermediary service organization must submit to the Division the
29 statement prescribed by the Division of Welfare and Supportive Services of the
30 Department of Health and Human Services pursuant to NRS 425.520. The
31 statement must be completed and signed by the applicant.
32 2. The Division shall include the statement required pursuant to subsection
33 1 in:
34 (a) The application or any other forms that must be submitted for the
35 issuance or renewal of the certificate; or
36 (b) A separate form prescribed by the Division.
37 3. A certificate to operate an intermediary service organization may not be
38 issued or renewed by the Division if the applicant:
39 (a) Fails to submit the statement required pursuant to subsection 1; or
40 (b) Indicates on the statement submitted pursuant to subsection 1 that the
41 applicant is subject to a court order for the support of a child and is not in
42 compliance with the order or a plan approved by the district attorney or other
43 public agency enforcing the order for the repayment of the amount owed
44 pursuant to the order.
45 4. If an applicant indicates on the statement submitted pursuant to
46 subsection 1 that the applicant is subject to a court order for the support of a
47 child and is not in compliance with the order or a plan approved by the district
48 attorney or other public agency enforcing the order for the repayment of the
49 amount owed pursuant to the order, the Division shall advise the applicant to
50 contact the district attorney or other public agency enforcing the order to
51 determine the actions that the applicant may take to satisfy the arrearage.
52 Sec. 66. Each application for a certificate to operate an intermediary
53 service organization must be accompanied by such fee as may be determined by

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 29
1 regulation of the Board. The Board may, by regulation, allow or require payment
2 of a fee for a certificate in installments and may fix the amount of each payment
3 and the date on which the payment is due.
4 Sec. 67. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6 and section 68 of
5 this act, each intermediary service organization shall, when applying for a
6 certificate or renewing a certificate, file with the Administrator of the Division of
7 Public and Behavioral Health a surety bond:
8 (a) If the intermediary service organization employs less than 7 employees, in
9 the amount of $5,000;
10 (b) If the intermediary service organization employs at least 7 but not more
11 than 25 employees, in the amount of $25,000; or
12 (c) If the intermediary service organization employs more than 25 employees,
13 in the amount of $50,000.
14 2. A bond filed pursuant to this section must be executed by the
15 intermediary service organization as principal and by a surety company as surety.
16 The bond must be payable to the Aging and Disability Services Division of the
17 Department of Health and Human Services and must be conditioned to provide
18 indemnification to an older patient whom the Attorney for the Rights of Older
19 Persons and Persons with a Physical Disability, an Intellectual Disability or a
20 Related Condition determines has suffered property damage as a result of any act
21 or failure to act by the intermediary service organization to protect the property of
22 the older patient.
23 3. Except when a surety is released, the surety bond must cover the period
24 of the initial certificate to operate or the period of the renewal, as appropriate.
25 4. A surety on any bond filed pursuant to this section may be released after
26 the surety gives 30 days’ written notice to the Administrator of the Division of
27 Public and Behavioral Health, but the release does not discharge or otherwise
28 affect any claim filed by an older patient for property damaged as a result of any
29 act or failure to act by the intermediary service organization to protect the
30 property of the older patient alleged to have occurred while the bond was in
31 effect.
32 5. A certificate is suspended by operation of law when the intermediary
33 service organization is no longer covered by a surety bond as required by this
34 section or by a substitute for the surety bond pursuant to section 68 of this act.
35 The Administrator of the Division of Public and Behavioral Health shall give the
36 intermediary service organization at least 20 days’ written notice before the
37 release of the surety or the substitute for the surety, to the effect that the
38 certificate will be suspended by operation of law until another surety bond or
39 substitute for the surety bond is filed in the same manner and amount as the bond
40 or substitute being terminated.
41 6. The requirement of filing a surety bond set forth in this section does not
42 apply to an intermediary service organization that is operated and maintained by
43 the State of Nevada or an agency thereof.
44 7. As used in this section, “older patient” means a patient who is 60 years of
45 age or older.
46 Sec. 68. 1. As a substitute for the surety bond required pursuant to
47 section 67 of this act, an intermediary service organization may deposit with any
48 bank or trust company authorized to do business in this State, upon approval
49 from the Administrator of the Division of Public and Behavioral Health:
50 (a) An obligation of a bank, savings and loan association, savings bank,
51 thrift company or credit union licensed to do business in this State;
52 (b) Bills, bonds, notes, debentures or other obligations of the United States or
53 any agency or instrumentality thereof, or guaranteed by the United States; or

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 30
1 (c) Any obligation of this State or any city, county, town, township, school
2 district or other instrumentality of this State, or guaranteed by this State, in an
3 aggregate amount, based upon principal amount or market value, whichever is
4 lower.
5 2. The obligations of a bank, savings and loan association, savings bank,
6 thrift company or credit union must be held to secure the same obligation as
7 would the surety bond required by section 67 of this act. With the approval of the
8 Administrator of the Division of Public and Behavioral Health, the depositor may
9 substitute other suitable obligations for those deposited, which must be assigned
10 to the Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health and
11 Human Services and are negotiable only upon approval by the Administrator of
12 the Aging and Disability Services Division.
13 3. Any interest or dividends earned on the deposit accrue to the account of
14 the depositor.
15 4. The deposit must be an amount at least equal to the surety bond required
16 by section 67 of this act and must state that the amount may not be withdrawn
17 except by direct and sole order of the Administrator of the Aging and Disability
18 Services Division.

39 Sec. 70. 1. The Division shall develop and implement a process by which
40 a person with a criminal history may petition the Division to review the criminal
41 history of the person to determine if the person’s criminal history will disqualify
42 the person from obtaining a certificate to operate an intermediary service
43 organization pursuant to section 62 of this act.
44 2. Not later than 90 days after a petition is submitted to the Division
45 pursuant to subsection 1, the Division shall inform the person of the
46 determination of the Division of whether the person’s criminal history will
47 disqualify the person from obtaining a certificate. The Division is not bound by
48 its determination of disqualification or qualification and may rescind such a
49 determination at any time.
50 3. The Division may provide instructions to a person who receives a
51 determination of disqualification to remedy the determination of disqualification.
52 A person may resubmit a petition pursuant to subsection 1 not earlier than 6

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 31
1 months after receiving instructions pursuant to this subsection if the person
2 remedies the determination of disqualification.
3 4. A person with a criminal history may petition the Division at any time,
4 including, without limitation, before obtaining any education or paying any fee
5 required to obtain a certificate from the Division.
6 5. A person may submit a new petition to the Division not earlier than 2
7 years after the final determination of the initial petition submitted to the Division.
8 6. The Division may impose a fee of up to $50 upon the person to fund the
9 administrative costs in complying with the provisions of this section. The Division
10 may waive such fees or allow such fees to be covered by funds from a scholarship
11 or grant.
12 7. The Division may post on its Internet website:
13 (a) The requirements to obtain a certificate from the Division; and
14 (b) A list of crimes, if any, that would disqualify a person from obtaining a
15 certificate from the Division.
16 8. The Division may request the criminal history record of a person who
17 petitions the Division for a determination pursuant to subsection 1. To the extent
18 consistent with federal law, if the Division makes such a request of a person, the
19 Division shall require the person to submit his or her criminal history record
20 which includes a report from:
21 (a) The Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History; and
22 (b) The Federal Bureau of Investigation.
23 9. A person who petitions the Division for a determination pursuant to
24 subsection 1 shall not submit false or misleading information to the Division.
25 10. The Division shall, on or before the 20th day of January, April, July
26 and October, submit to the Director of the Legislative Counsel Bureau in an

28 (a) The number of petitions submitted to the Division pursuant to subsection
29 1;
30 (b) The number of determinations of disqualification made by the Division
31 pursuant to subsection 1;
32 (c) The reasons for such determinations; and
33 (d) Any other information that is requested by the Director or which the
34 Division determines would be helpful.
35 11. The Director shall transmit a compilation of the information received
36 pursuant to subsection 10 to the Legislative Commission quarterly, unless
37 otherwise directed by the Commission.

51 3. The holder of a certificate to operate an intermediary service
52 organization is not required to obtain the information described in subsection 1,
53 other than the information described in paragraph (c) of subsection 1, from an

1 employee, employee of a temporary employment service or independent

20 4. The holder of a certificate to operate an intermediary service
21 organization shall ensure that the information concerning the background and
22 personal history of each employee, employee of a temporary employment service
23 or independent contractor who works at or for the intermediary service
24 organization is completed as soon as practicable and at least once every 5 years
25 after the date of the initial investigation. The holder of the certificate shall, when
26 required:
27 (a) Obtain one set of fingerprints from the employee, employee of the
28 temporary employment service or independent contractor;
29 (b) Obtain written authorization from the employee, employee of the
30 temporary employment service or independent contractor to forward the
31 fingerprints obtained pursuant to paragraph (a) to the Central Repository for
32 Nevada Records of Criminal History for submission to the Federal Bureau of
33 Investigation for its report; and
34 (c) Submit the fingerprints to the Central Repository for Nevada Records of
35 Criminal History or, if the fingerprints were submitted electronically, obtain
36 proof of electronic submission of the fingerprints to the Central Repository for
37 Nevada Records of Criminal History.
38 5. Upon receiving fingerprints submitted pursuant to this section, the
39 Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History shall determine
40 whether the employee, employee of the temporary employment service or
41 independent contractor has been convicted of a crime listed in subsection 1 of
42 section 85 of this act and immediately inform the Division and the holder of the
43 certificate to operate an intermediary service organization for which the person
44 works whether the employee, employee of the temporary employment service or
45 independent contractor has been convicted of such a crime.
46 6. The Central Repository for Nevada Records of Criminal History may
47 impose a fee upon an intermediary service organization that submits fingerprints

49 intermediary service organization may recover from the employee or independent
50 contractor whose fingerprints are submitted not more than one-half of the fee
51 imposed by the Central Repository. If the intermediary service organization
52 requires the employee or independent contractor to pay for any part of the fee
53 imposed by the Central Repository, it shall allow the employee or independent

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 36
1 contractor to pay the amount through periodic payments. The intermediary
2 service organization may require a temporary employment service which employs
3 a temporary employee whose fingerprints are submitted to pay the fee imposed by
4 the Central Repository. An intermediary service organization shall notify a
5 temporary employment service if a person employed by the temporary
6 employment service is determined to be ineligible to provide services to the

8 conducted pursuant to this section.
9 7. Unless a greater penalty is provided by law, a person who willfully

11 the background and personal history of the person pursuant to this section that
12 would disqualify the person from employment, including, without limitation, a
13 conviction of a crime listed in subsection 1 of section 85 of this act, is guilty of a

44 Sec. 85. In addition to the grounds listed in section 75 of this act, the
