52 exposure, or any other sexually related crime that is punished as a felony;

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 38
1 (d) Prostitution, solicitation, lewdness or indecent exposure, or any other

4 (e) Abuse or neglect of a child or contributory delinquency;
5 (f) A violation of any federal or state law regulating the possession,
6 distribution or use of any controlled substance or any dangerous drug as defined
7 in chapter 454 of NRS, within the past 7 years;
8 (g) A violation of any provision of NRS 200.5099 or 200.50995;

16 Sec. 86. 1. If an intermediary service organization violates any provision
17 related to its certification, including, without limitation, any provision of sections
18 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act or any condition, standard or regulation adopted by
19 the Board, the Division, in accordance with the regulations adopted pursuant to
20 section 87 of this act, may, as it deems appropriate:
21 (a) Prohibit the intermediary service organization from providing services
22 pursuant to section 60 of this act until it determines that the intermediary service
23 organization has corrected the violation;
24 (b) Impose an administrative penalty of not more than $1,000 per day for
25 each violation, together with interest thereon at a rate not to exceed 10 percent
26 per annum; and
27 (c) Appoint temporary management to oversee the operation of the
28 intermediary service organization and to ensure the health and safety of the
29 persons for whom the intermediary service organization performs services, until:
30 (1) It determines that the intermediary service organization has corrected
31 the violation and has management which is capable of ensuring continued
32 compliance with the applicable statutes, conditions, standards and regulations; or
33 (2) Improvements are made to correct the violation.
34 2. If the intermediary service organization fails to pay any administrative
35 penalty imposed pursuant to paragraph (b) of subsection 1, the Division may:
36 (a) Suspend the certificate to operate an intermediary service organization
37 which is held by the intermediary service organization until the administrative
38 penalty is paid; and
39 (b) Collect court costs, reasonable attorney’s fees and other costs incurred to
40 collect the administrative penalty.
41 3. The Division may require any intermediary service organization that
42 violates any provision of sections 59 to 90, inclusive, of this act, or any condition,
43 standard or regulation adopted by the Board, to make any improvements
44 necessary to correct the violation.
45 4. Any money collected as administrative penalties pursuant to this section
46 must be accounted for separately and used to protect the health or property of the
47 persons for whom the intermediary service organization performs services in
48 accordance with applicable federal standards.
49 Sec. 87. The Board shall adopt regulations establishing the criteria for the
50 imposition of each sanction prescribed by section 86 of this act. These regulations
51 must:
52 1. Prescribe the circumstances and manner in which each sanction applies;

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 39
1 2. Minimize the time between identification of a violation and the
2 imposition of a sanction;
3 3. Provide for the imposition of incrementally more severe sanctions for
4 repeated or uncorrected violations; and
5 4. Provide for less severe sanctions for lesser violations of applicable state
6 statutes, conditions, standards or regulations.
7 Sec. 88. 1. When the Division intends to deny, suspend or revoke a
8 certificate to operate an intermediary service organization, or to impose any
9 sanction prescribed by section 86 of this act, the Division shall give reasonable
10 notice to the holder of the certificate by certified mail. The notice must contain
11 the legal authority, jurisdiction and reasons for the action to be taken. Notice is
12 not required if the Division finds that the public health requires immediate
13 action. In that case, the Division may order a summary suspension of a certificate
14 or impose any sanction prescribed by section 86 of this act, pending proceedings
15 for revocation or other action.
16 2. If a person wants to contest the action of the Division, the person must
17 file an appeal pursuant to regulations adopted by the Board.
18 3. Upon receiving notice of an appeal, the Division shall hold a hearing
19 pursuant to regulations adopted by the Board.
20 4. The Board shall adopt such regulations as are necessary to carry out the
21 provisions of this section.
22 Sec. 89. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2 of section 62 of

29 Division.

31 certain date and in a certain place, operate and maintain the intermediary service

9 facility for the care of adults during the day, residential facility for groups or home
10 for individual residential care must annually receive training to recognize and
11 prevent the abuse of older persons before the license to operate such a facility [,
12 agency] or home may be renewed.
13 3. If an applicant or licensee who is required by this section to obtain training
14 is not a natural person, the person in charge of the facility [, agency] or home must
15 receive the training required by this section.
16 4. An administrator or other person in charge of a facility for intermediate
17 care, facility for skilled nursing, [agency to provide personal care services in the
18 home,] facility for the care of adults during the day, residential facility for groups or
19 home for individual residential care must receive training to recognize and prevent
20 the abuse of older persons before the facility [, agency] or home provides care to a
21 person and annually thereafter.
22 5. An employee who will provide care to a person in a facility for
23 intermediate care, facility for skilled nursing, [agency to provide personal care
24 services in the home,] facility for the care of adults during the day, residential
25 facility for groups or home for individual residential care must receive training to
26 recognize and prevent the abuse of older persons before the employee provides care
27 to a person in the facility [, agency] or home and annually thereafter.
28 6. The topics of instruction that must be included in the training required by
29 this section must include, without limitation:
30 (a) Recognizing the abuse of older persons, including sexual abuse and
31 violations of NRS 200.5091 to 200.50995, inclusive;
32 (b) Responding to reports of the alleged abuse of older persons, including
33 sexual abuse and violations of NRS 200.5091 to 200.50995, inclusive; and
34 (c) Instruction concerning the federal, state and local laws, and any changes to
35 those laws, relating to:
36 (1) The abuse of older persons; and
37 (2) Facilities for intermediate care, facilities for skilled nursing, [agencies
38 to provide personal care services in the home,] facilities for the care of adults
39 during the day, residential facilities for groups or homes for individual residential
40 care, as applicable for the person receiving the training.
41 7. The facility for intermediate care, facility for skilled nursing, [agency to
42 provide personal care services in the home,] facility for the care of adults during the
43 day, residential facility for groups or home for individual residential care is
44 responsible for the costs related to the training required by this section.
45 8. The administrator of a facility for intermediate care, facility for skilled
46 nursing or residential facility for groups who is licensed pursuant to chapter 654 of
47 NRS shall ensure that each employee of the facility who provides care to residents
48 has obtained the training required by this section. If an administrator or employee
49 of a facility or home does not obtain the training required by this section, the
50 Division shall notify the Board of Examiners for Long-Term Care Administrators
51 that the administrator is in violation of this section.
52 9. The holder of a license to operate a facility for intermediate care, facility
53 for skilled nursing, [agency to provide personal care services in the home,] facility

1 for the care of adults during the day, residential facility for groups or home for

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 49
1 NOTICE TO TENANTS OF THE PROPERTY
2
3 Foreclosure proceedings against this property have started, and a notice of
4 sale of the property to the highest bidder has been issued.
5
6 You may either: (1) terminate your lease or rental agreement and move out;
7 or (2) remain and possibly be subject to eviction proceedings under chapter
8 40 of the Nevada Revised Statutes. Any subtenants may also be subject to
9 eviction proceedings.
10
11 Between now and the date of the sale, you may be evicted if you fail to pay
12 rent or live up to your other obligations to the landlord.
13
14 After the date of the sale, you may be evicted if you fail to pay rent or live
15 up to your other obligations to the successful bidder, in accordance with
16 chapter 118A of the Nevada Revised Statutes.
17
18 Under the Nevada Revised Statutes, eviction proceedings may begin
19 against you after you have been given a notice to surrender.
20
21 If the property is sold and you pay rent by the week or another period of
22 time that is shorter than 1 month, you should generally receive notice after
23 not less than the number of days in that period of time.
24
25 If the property is sold and you pay rent by the month or any other period of
26 time that is 1 month or longer, you should generally receive notice at least
27 60 days in advance.
28
29 Under Nevada Revised Statutes 40.280, notice must generally be served on
30 you pursuant to chapter 40 of the Nevada Revised Statutes.
31
32 If the property is sold and a landlord, successful bidder or subsequent
33 purchaser files an eviction action against you in court, you will be served
34 with a summons and complaint and have the opportunity to respond.
35 Eviction actions may result in temporary evictions, permanent evictions, the
36 awarding of damages pursuant to Nevada Revised Statutes 40.360 or some
37 combination of those results.
38
39 Under the Justice Court Rules of Civil Procedure:
40 (1) You will be given at least 10 days to answer a summons and
41 complaint;
42 (2) If you do not file an answer, an order evicting you by default may
43 be obtained against you;
44 (3) A hearing regarding a temporary eviction may be called as soon as
45 11 days after you are served with the summons and complaint; and
46 (4) A hearing regarding a permanent eviction may be called as soon as
47 20 days after you are served with the summons and complaint.
48
49 4. The sheriff shall not conduct a sale of the property on execution or deliver
50 the judgment debtor’s property to the judgment creditor if the judgment debtor or

52 section and NRS 21.075 and 21.076.

18 issued pursuant to this section must be renewed:
19 (a) Every 5 years; and
20 (b) Whenever the person changes his or her employment to perform work for
21 an employer other than the employer for which the person’s current work card was
22 issued.

31 Investigation to determine the criminal history of the applicant.

9 Sec. 113. NRS 200.5093 is hereby amended to read as follows:
10 200.5093 1. Any person who is described in subsection 4 and who, in a
11 professional or occupational capacity, knows or has reasonable cause to believe that
12 an older person or vulnerable person has been abused, neglected, exploited, isolated
13 or abandoned shall:
14 (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, report the abuse, neglect,
15 exploitation, isolation or abandonment of the older person or vulnerable person to:
16 (1) The local office of the Aging and Disability Services Division of the
17 Department of Health and Human Services;
18 (2) A police department or sheriff’s office; or
19 (3) A toll-free telephone service designated by the Aging and Disability
20 Services Division of the Department of Health and Human Services; and
21 (b) Make such a report as soon as reasonably practicable but not later than 24
22 hours after the person knows or has reasonable cause to believe that the older
23 person or vulnerable person has been abused, neglected, exploited, isolated or
24 abandoned.
25 2. If a person who is required to make a report pursuant to subsection 1 knows
26 or has reasonable cause to believe that the abuse, neglect, exploitation, isolation or
27 abandonment of the older person or vulnerable person involves an act or omission
28 of the Aging and Disability Services Division, another division of the Department
29 of Health and Human Services or a law enforcement agency, the person shall make
30 the report to an agency other than the one alleged to have committed the act or
31 omission.

33 report to the Aging and Disability Services Division of the Department of Health
34 and Human Services and the Unit for the Investigation and Prosecution of Crimes.

52 person in charge of a hospital or similar institution upon notification of the

28 memorandum may be prepared from those public books and public records. Any
29 such copies, abstracts or memoranda may be used to supply the general public with

31 the advantage of the governmental entity or of the general public. This section does
32 not supersede or in any manner affect the federal laws governing copyrights or
33 enlarge, diminish or affect in any other manner the rights of a person in any written
34 book or record which is copyrighted pursuant to federal law.
35 2. A governmental entity may not reject a book or record which is
36 copyrighted solely because it is copyrighted.
37 3. A governmental entity that has legal custody or control of a public book or
38 record shall not deny a request made pursuant to subsection 1 to inspect or copy or
39 receive a copy of a public book or record on the basis that the requested public
40 book or record contains information that is confidential if the governmental entity
41 can redact, delete, conceal or separate, including, without limitation, electronically,
42 the confidential information from the information included in the public book or
43 record that is not otherwise confidential.
44 4. If requested, a governmental entity shall provide a copy of a public record
45 in an electronic format by means of an electronic medium. Nothing in this
46 subsection requires a governmental entity to provide a copy of a public record in an
47 electronic format or by means of an electronic medium if:
48 (a) The public record:
49 (1) Was not created or prepared in an electronic format; and
50 (2) Is not available in an electronic format; or
51 (b) Providing the public record in an electronic format or by means of an
52 electronic medium would:
53 (1) Give access to proprietary software; or

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 68
1 (2) Require the production of information that is confidential and that
2 cannot be redacted, deleted, concealed or separated from information that is not
3 otherwise confidential.
4 5. An officer, employee or agent of a governmental entity who has legal
5 custody or control of a public record:
6 (a) Shall not refuse to provide a copy of that public record in the medium that
7 is requested because the officer, employee or agent has already prepared or would
8 prefer to provide the copy in a different medium.
9 (b) Except as otherwise provided in NRS 239.030, shall, upon request, prepare
10 the copy of the public record and shall not require the person who has requested the
11 copy to prepare the copy himself or herself.

51 assistance under Medicaid.

48 Sec. 123. NRS 427A.175 is hereby amended to read as follows:
49 427A.175 1. Within 1 year after an older patient sustains damage to his or
50 her property as a result of any act or failure to act by a facility for intermediate care,
51 a facility for skilled nursing, a residential facility for groups, a home for individual
52 residential care, an agency to provide personal care services in the home, an

Assembly Amendment No. 451 to Assembly Bill No. 519 Page 70
1 provide nursing in the home in protecting the property, the older patient may file a
2 verified complaint with the Division setting forth the details of the damage.
3 2. Upon receiving a verified complaint pursuant to subsection 1, the
4 Administrator shall investigate the complaint and attempt to settle the matter
5 through arbitration, mediation or negotiation.
6 3. If a settlement is not reached pursuant to subsection 2, the facility, home,
7 agency, organization or older patient may request a hearing before the Attorney for
8 the Rights of Older Persons and Persons with a Physical Disability, an Intellectual
9 Disability or a Related Condition. If requested, the Attorney for the Rights of Older
10 Persons and Persons with a Physical Disability, an Intellectual Disability or a
11 Related Condition shall conduct a hearing to determine whether the facility, home,
12 agency, pool or organization is liable for damages to the patient. If the Attorney for
13 the Rights of Older Persons and Persons with a Physical Disability, an Intellectual
14 Disability or a Related Condition determines that the facility, home, agency, pool or
15 organization is liable for damages to the patient, the Attorney for the Rights of
16 Older Persons and Persons with a Physical Disability, an Intellectual Disability or a
17 Related Condition shall order the amount of the surety bond pursuant to NRS
18 449.065 or section 24 or 67 of this act, as applicable, or the substitute for the
19 surety bond necessary to pay for the damages pursuant to NRS 449.067 or section
20 25 or 68 of this act, as applicable, to be released to the Division. The Division shall
21 pay any such amount to the older patient or the estate of the older patient.
